British General Election Begins; Fierce Competition Among Political Parties; 615 Members of Parliament Must Be Elected; Ruling Party Expected to Lose Seats; Female Voters Outnumber Men 34

(London) Britain began voting today to elect members of the House of Commons. Although the government is optimistic about the future, at least four cabinet ministers are at risk of losing their seats, namely Macdonald (Labour), who has served as Prime Minister three times and is currently the Lord President of the Council, Scottish Secretary Sir Colin Coote (Liberal), Minister of Health Sir Kingsley Wood (Conservative), and Minister of Agriculture and Fisheries Elliot (Conservative). The opposition Labour Party is increasingly optimistic, believing that many of the leaders who lost in the 1931 general election have a chance of returning to Parliament this time. If so, the Labour Party's opposition to the government in Parliament could greatly increase. The sentiments of the various parties are roughly as follows:

The government believes that victory is assured, but acknowledges that its majority will inevitably decrease. The opposition Labour Party believes that victory is "extremely lucky," but is confident that the number of seats it wins will allow it to make a substantial voice in the new Parliament. The Liberal opposition party believes that it can play a pivotal role in the election. The nation's policies, especially foreign policy, will now be tested on the world and the voters, as this election is a direct result of the East African War. The government's decision to implement sanctions against Italy to uphold Britain's support for the League of Nations and oppose Italy's plan to expand its colonies has caused a serious split in the Labour Party. By holding elections at this time, the government is not only acting in the party's interest but also seeking a new mandate from the voters for the international situation, so as to continue to support the League of Nations and pursue a policy of strengthening national defense in accordance with international developments. The Labour Party has always advocated peace, but party members have sharply divided opinions on the issue of implementing sanctions to maintain peace. The Liberal Party, on the other hand, finds that most of its foreign policy aligns with the government, and many are taking advantage of the situation to switch sides. The government has now shifted the nation's attention to foreign affairs, causing domestic issues such as unemployment and social welfare to be neglected. The opposition parties naturally use these issues as weapons in their struggles. In short, the opposition parties have indeed made much progress in the constituencies in recent months. It is generally predicted that the government's majority will be between 100 and 250 seats. The opposition parties' chances have increased slightly during the election campaign in the past week. (Fourteenth Reuters Telegram)

(London) A total of 615 members of the House of Commons must be elected, but there are no contests in 40 seats, which have already been decided. Prime Minister Baldwin is among them. Polling stations opened as early as 7:00 AM this morning, and many others started operating from 8:00 AM. Voting will continue until 8:00 or 9:00 PM, depending on local conditions. The weather is good today, with occasional sunshine. Baldwin drove from his residence at 10 Downing Street to Westminster to vote at 10:30 AM.

Experts from all parties say that the government is certain to be elected, but its current majority of 404 seats will inevitably be greatly reduced.

Since the last general election, the number of voters has increased by 1.5 million, and their political opinions are difficult to discern. Female voters outnumber men by 1.75 million. It is expected that the results of the 225 rural constituencies, totaling 232 seats, will be known tonight. The results of the remaining areas, except for a few, will be known tomorrow night. The British Broadcasting Corporation will broadcast the results as they are received from 10:00 PM tonight to 4:00 AM tomorrow morning.

All parties expect the government to suffer the greatest losses in the 225 rural constituencies. In the last parliament, the government party held 197 of these 232 seats, and the opposition party held 35 seats. In the 1929 parliament, the Conservative Party held 77 seats, the Labour Party held 138 seats, the Liberal Party held 14 seats, and independents held 3 seats.

Four cabinet ministers, including Macdonald, are at risk of losing their seats. Another four cabinet ministers, namely Lord Hailsham, the Lord Chancellor, Lord Halifax, the Secretary of State for War, Lord Londonderry, the Lord Privy Seal, and Lord Zetland, the Secretary of State for India, are not affected by the election because they are members of the House of Lords. All four are affiliated with the Conservative Party. (Fourteenth Reuters Telegram)

British Voters: Over 25 Million. Number of Seats Held by Each Party in the Last House of Commons 35

(London) Tomorrow is the date for the general election of the British House of Commons. This is an unprecedented grand showdown of British political parties in four years. According to British election law, both men and women who are 21 years of age or older have the right to vote. Therefore, it is predicted that the number of voters will be over 25 million. The current British House of Commons was elected on October 27, 1931, and the distribution of seats for each party is as follows:

(1) Government Party

Conservative Party: 471

National Liberal Party: 68

National Labour Party: 13

Independents: 2

(2) Opposition Party

Labour Party: 52

Liberal Party: 4

Independents: 5

Total: 615

From the above table, the National Cabinet holds an overwhelming majority of 554 seats in the House of Commons, and therefore has been able to govern for four years, with its foundation unshaken. However, judging from the by-elections and municipal council elections in recent years, the opposition Labour Party has often been victorious. The National Government can no longer obtain the majority support it received four years ago, which is indeed due to failures in domestic policy. Therefore, in this general election, the Labour Party may have hopes of making a comeback. Optimists in the Conservative Party predict that the Labour Party will only be able to obtain 175 seats, which is more than 120 seats more than in the last election. If this is the case, the Government Party can still maintain an absolute majority. However, according to the speculation of Lord Stobart, a Labour Party senator, the Labour Party can win a majority of 30 to 40 seats, that is, the number of seats obtained is often more than 330. In general, the following estimates are most likely: the Labour Party will win between 200 and 230 seats, the opposition independents will win 10 seats, the Samuelite Liberals will win 10 to 20 seats, and the Government Party will win 350 to 400 seats, which is still a majority of 100 to 160 seats. However, there are a large number of voters in the British election who do not participate in voting, of which 1.5 million voters do not easily reveal their attitude during the election period. Therefore, it is difficult to foresee what the result will be. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(London) The general election of the British House of Commons was held today. The final result of the vote will depend on the number of votes of the Liberal Party. The Liberal Party is divided into two factions, one led by Home Secretary Simon, which belongs to the government faction, and the other is the Samuelite faction, which is the anti-government faction. The two factions have a total of 211 candidate members, of which 41 are from the Simon faction and 178 are from the Samuelite faction. In each constituency where the Simonite Liberals have nominated candidates, the confrontation between the Government Party and the opposition Labour Party is very clear. However, in the areas where the Samuelite Liberals have nominated candidates, a triangular struggle has been created. The Samuelite faction is probably only able to obtain a few seats, but because the votes of the opposition are scattered, it is enough to allow the Government Party to obtain benefits. As for the constituencies where the Liberal Party has not nominated candidates, the Liberal Party advises voters to vote for candidates who accept the "Programme for Peace and Economic Reconstruction." Only about 20 Conservative Party candidates have accepted this programme, and only one-third of Labour Party candidates have accepted it. For this reason, in the majority of constituencies where the Liberal Party has not nominated candidates, most Liberal voters will be at a loss as to what to do. The number of votes of these voters is estimated to be nearly 1.5 million, and their voting attitude is questionable. Therefore, it is difficult to predict what the election result will be. According to various speculations, the Conservative Party will still win a majority, but it may be reduced by 100 seats compared to its original seats. If so, whether the National Cabinet can continue to exist will depend on the attitude of the Simonite Liberals and the Conservative Party "Diehards" (i.e., the right-wing Conservative Party led by Churchill). If the Simonite Liberals and the right-wing Conservatives leave the Government Party, the Cabinet will not be able to sustain itself. The Simonite Liberals advocate free trade, while the right-wing Conservatives advocate extreme protectionist tariffs and imperial isolation policies. The two are extremely opposed, and it will be very difficult for the government to mediate between them at that time. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(London) The election campaign of each party has become increasingly heated. 1,300 candidates are today displaying their debating talents, making their final speeches. The Labour Party has been wary of elections since 1924, fearing that a similar Zinoviev Letter will appear again, leading to the collapse of the first Labour Cabinet. However, their concerns have not yet become a reality. The Labour Party candidates attempted to force the Government spokesperson to explain Baldwin's defense spending, but to no avail, because the Government candidates refused to discuss this issue. (National dispatch on the 13th)

The Anti-British Movement in Egypt: The Situation Remains Serious; More Deaths and Injuries in Yesterday's Riot 36

Cairo: The situation in Cairo remains serious. Last night, the public took to the streets in demonstrations, protesting against the government and Britain's attitude towards the Egyptian constitution, causing disturbances. There was more trouble this morning. About 1,000 rioters, each holding sticks and other objects, attempted to enter Cairo from Giza. 200 policemen went to stop them. As a result, a major conflict broke out. The police fired shots into the air to no avail. A policeman, for the sake of self-defense, drew his pistol and shot down four attackers, killing one and injuring three. The crowd was frightened and scattered. The Egyptian government decided that if university students do not resume classes on November 16, all universities will be closed for a week starting from the 17th. The government is now doing its best to maintain order, and infantry are stationed on all major streets. It is reported that in the riots of the past two days, a total of three people have died and 147 have been injured, half of whom are policemen. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Cairo: Riots broke out again today, with clashes between police and students, resulting in the death of one student and serious injuries to nine others. Thus, a total of three people have died and 200 have been injured. The authorities are deeply concerned that this disturbance may spread to various provinces, and are now investigating the instigator. Italian influence is quite strong in Egypt, which makes the authorities pay more attention. (National dispatch on the 14th)

Cairo: Riots broke out again tonight. The public attacked police stations with glass bottles, bricks, and other sharp objects. The police were unable to suppress them and fired shots, resulting in many deaths and injuries. Earlier, the National Autonomy Party held a meeting and passed two resolutions: (1) do not cooperate with the British, and (3) demand the resignation of the Lessim government. This government was established on November 15, 1934. During the day, a mob smashed the windows of the British consulate and attacked a large Greek store, and committed other atrocities. The riots stemmed from a speech made by British Foreign Secretary Hoare at the Lord Mayor of London's annual banquet last Saturday. The Foreign Secretary stated that in the section on British-Egyptian relations, Britain had advised Egypt not to restore the constitutions of 1923 and 1930, because one had already proven to be unimplementable and the other had proven to be unsatisfactory to public opinion. However, the Foreign Secretary denied that Britain opposed the restoration of a constitution suitable for Egypt's needs. Once the news that Britain did not want Egypt to restore its constitution spread, politicians were greatly indignant. Last night, the National Autonomy Party held a meeting and resolved to cancel the assistance given to Prime Minister Lessim because he did not disregard Britain's advice. As a result, the political situation became increasingly turbulent, and there were riots yesterday. (Reuters dispatch on the 13th)

(London) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and British Ambassador to Italy Drummond negotiated to reduce the tense atmosphere in the Mediterranean. According to the news here today, there were many disputes in the conversation. Drummond first suggested that Italy reduce its troops stationed in Libya to 45,000, and Britain also withdrew the two ships, Hoot and Lennen, currently stationed in the Mediterranean. Mussolini wanted to expand the scope of the negotiations, suggesting that the British Mediterranean fleet should be limited to 440,000 tons, and 340,000 tons in peacetime. Mussolini also suggested that Italy control the eastern end of the Mediterranean, from the south of Sicily to Istanbul in Turkey, while Britain controls the western end. However, according to reliable sources, if Italy formally proposes this suggestion to divide the "sphere of influence," it will definitely be rejected. (National News Agency dispatch on the 13th)

Their suffering is no less than that of consumers. Moreover, non-essential goods such as silk fabrics and leather goods still cannot increase in price. Only those who purchase goods with silver not only do not pay a higher price but even pay a lower price. Despite efforts to prohibit it, it cannot be stopped. The reason for this is that business is sluggish and unsustainable. However, the fact that banks generally do not provide loans, resulting in a lack of capital turnover, is a major factor. International Commercial Telegraph — Reuters Special Commercial Report, November 14 — 79

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price fell by one and a half pence today, to 141 shillings and four and a half pence.

British Silver: The London silver market continued to be stable, with prices remaining unchanged. Spot price was 29 and 3125/10000 pence, and futures price was 29 and 10625/10000 pence. American purchases and speculator trading were both active.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was $4.923125, which was lower by 0.0625 compared to yesterday's closing rate. At noon, it fell by 375/10000 to $4.919375. At 2 p.m., it rebounded by 25/10000 to $4.921875.

British-French: The opening rate rose by one pound to 74.72 francs. At noon, it fell by six centimes. At 2 p.m., it returned to 74.72 francs.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened high by five points. Although there was selling from Alexandria, the cotton price continued to rise by twelve points. The reasons for the soaring market conditions were: (1) strong domestic fundamentals, (2) improved exports, (3) favorable weather for winter crops, (4) good demand from the industry, and (5) few short-covering activities.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened with a price increase of 1.125 points due to favorable news from Liverpool and South America. Later, due to the domestic weather report, the price continued to rise by half a point. Feed grains also opened with an increase of one to 1.375 points. The price immediately fell due to short-covering activities.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was relatively stable this morning. At 1 p.m., the December futures price was 5 shillings and 11 pence, up by 0.75 points.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market also rose. At 1 p.m., the January futures price rose by five points to 6.39.

Rubber

London: The rubber market opened with a stable price. The trading price for January-March futures was 6.4375 pence, which was the same as yesterday's closing price. There was no change at noon.

New York: The rubber market opened quite stable due to the favorable news from London. The price was high by five points. Speculative demand was active during the telegraphing, and the industry was also actively buying. The market price continued to rise by eleven points.

Securities

New York: The securities market opened relatively firm this morning. Railroad stocks rose the most sharply because the Pennsylvania Railroad issued dividends. Mining stocks also rose sharply. Although there was profit-taking, it was only temporary. The market price immediately rebounded. Entertainment stock prices also rose. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks opened at 144.13, up by 54 points.

Educational Broadcasting Special

How do wind, rain, thunder, lightning, dew, frost, hail, and snow occur? 80

(Lectures to the national public on November 4th and 6th)

— Professor Huan Yong of Central University

(I) The topic of this lecture is "How do wind, rain, thunder, lightning, frost, hail, and snow occur?" It is not an easy task to compress such a complex topic into a very short time. I will reluctantly divide it into two lectures. Today, I will first talk about how wind, rain, and thunder occur.

What is wind? Wind is a flow of air. The Earth's surface is surrounded by a layer of air of considerable thickness. In ordinary times, we perceive air as colorless and odorless, and sometimes we hardly notice its existence. However, when it flows, it can sometimes make a whooshing sound. If we can acknowledge the existence of wind, then we must acknowledge the existence of air.

During the hot summer, we need a gentle breeze. In winter, we fear the bitter north wind. How does wind actually occur, and why are its properties so different?

We see that water is constantly flowing. Its direction of flow is always from high to low. The so-called nature of water is to flow downward. Water does not inherently have a downward-flowing nature, but because it is subject to the Earth's gravitational pull, it has no choice but to flow from high to low until it reaches a level. In other words, the flow of water is also due to water pressure. Water at a high altitude has a greater downward pressure, while water at a low altitude has a lower downward pressure. The greater pressure overcomes the lesser pressure, so water at a high altitude has to flow to a low altitude. However, this water pressure is still produced by the Earth's gravitational pull.

Although the substance of air is thin, it is also subject to the Earth's gravitational pull. Therefore, it also has downward pressure, which is what we call air pressure. The flow of air is the same as the flow of water, flowing from areas of high pressure to areas of low pressure. Weather maps published by meteorological stations and weather forecasts published in newspapers often use terms such as "high-pressure" and "low-pressure." High pressure is where the air pressure is higher, and low pressure is where the air pressure is lower. In high-pressure areas, wind tends to flow outward, while in low-pressure areas, wind tends to flow inward. We humans live in the lower layer of the air, just like fish living on the seabed in the deep sea. Although we cannot see the height and thickness of the air layer, we can see the direction of airflow or wind from the level of air pressure.

Usually, meteorological stations or observatories observe the wind by looking at its direction and speed. The direction of airflow is mostly from high-pressure areas to low-pressure areas. Usually, wind direction is described using the four cardinal directions (east, south, west, and north), or by adding southeast, southwest, northeast, and northwest to form eight directions, or even more precisely with sixteen directions, or even thirty-two directions. As for the strength of the wind, it depends on the difference between high and low air pressure. The greater the difference in air pressure between two places, the stronger the wind; the smaller the difference, the weaker the wind. As for the temperature of the wind, it depends on its source. It is hot if it comes from a hot place, and it is cold if it comes from a cold place. For example, our winter wind mostly blows from the north. The weather in the north is cold, so the wind is also cold.

Air often contains water vapor. The source of this water vapor is mostly evaporated from the surface of the sea, the surface of the river, and even the humid land surface. Like air, water vapor is usually invisible. When water vapor cools, it re-condenses into water droplets. Small water droplets remain in the air due to the buoyancy of the air. This is what we call fog and clouds. Low-lying water droplets are called fog, and high-lying water droplets are called clouds. These are all tiny water droplets in the air. When the water droplets become larger, the air cannot support them, and they will fall down. This is what we call rain. Therefore, rain is when water vapor rises, is cooled, condenses into large water droplets, and then falls down.

As for thunder and lightning, they are originally the same phenomenon. The sound we hear is called thunder, and the light we see is called lightning. These are all variations of electricity. Water vapor in the air, especially in clouds, can generate and carry a large amount of electricity. Air is a relatively poor conductor of electricity. When electricity in the sky wants to reach the ground, or when electricity from one cloud wants to reach another cloud, it encounters the resistance of the air, which can produce light and sound. However, sound travels slowly and light travels quickly, so we often see lightning first and then hear thunder. During heavy rainstorms in the summer, the electrical charge in the air is very strong. Sometimes, it can pass through trees, houses, and even human bodies, causing lightning strikes. Nowadays, tall buildings are mostly equipped with lightning rods, using metal wires to conduct the current and prevent it from passing through the building. Because metal is a better conductor of electricity than buildings, the electricity travels through the metal wire, and the building can avoid lightning strikes and even being damaged. Thunder and lightning are a very common natural phenomenon and are by no means controlled by gods in the dark, as some people think.

The above briefly describes the causes of wind, rain, thunder, and lightning. How dew, frost, hail, and snow occur will be discussed next time.

(II) Today, I will continue from the last time to talk about how dew, frost, hail, and snow occur. Last time, I talked about how water on the ground or sea is heated and evaporates into vapor, which stays in the air and is called water vapor. When water vapor cools, it newly condenses into water droplets. Small water droplets float in the air and become clouds. Larger water droplets float near the ground and become fog. If the water droplets are too large, the air cannot support them, and they fall directly down as rain.

The changes of water vapor in the air are not limited to these three types of clouds, fog, and rain. When the sun sets on summer evenings, the ground temperature slowly decreases. The air temperature is often slightly higher than the ground temperature in an instant. The water vapor in the air is not low enough yet and has not reached the point of condensation, but the ground is cool enough. The water vapor in the air can condense into water droplets when it encounters the surface of the ground or grass and plants. This is called dew. Dew and fog are essentially the same thing, but one condenses on the ground, and the other condenses in the air. The two cannot coexist at the same time. If there is fog, there will be no dew; if there is dew, there will be no fog. In foggy weather, the ground is moistened by the fog droplets in the air and can also become moist, but that is not dew. Whenever there is cloudy weather, the clouds can prevent the ground from dissipating heat, and the temperature does not easily decrease, so dew cannot form. Dew also does not easily form when there is a strong wind.

Frost and dew are essentially the same thing. The ancients said, "Dew congeals into frost." Frost is not congealed from dew. However, when water vapor condenses on the ground, if the temperature is above the freezing point, it becomes dew; if it is below the freezing point, it becomes frost. This is entirely due to the difference in temperature. It is not that water vapor first congeals into dew and then congeals into frost. Dew mostly forms in summer and autumn, while frost forms in late winter and early spring. Whenever frost forms in the evening, the temperature must have dropped below the freezing point. Delicate plants cannot withstand the invasion of frost, so they inevitably lose their leaves and turn yellow when frost falls.

Snow is to rain as frost is to dew. In the high altitude, if the water vapor's temperature decreases and is above the freezing point, it forms clouds and rain. If the temperature decreases and is below the freezing point, the water vapor will condense into snow. Snow is directly condensed from water vapor, not formed from water droplets or raindrops. Sometimes water vapor condenses into fine ice needles that can also remain in the air, such as the cirrus clouds that are commonly seen.

Snow often falls in winter, while hail often falls in summer. Snow is a tiny flower, while hail is a block of ice. Snow often falls in winter when it is cold, and because the low temperature at that time is sufficient to kill pests on the ground, people often call it auspicious snow. Hail often falls in the hot summer when crops are growing. Whenever hail falls, it often causes disasters. The nature of snow and hail is so different, so the circumstances of their occurrence are also very different. Snowflakes are directly condensed from water vapor, while hail is a mixture of snowflakes and raindrops. During the summer, the ground temperature is hot, and the air rises, causing strong convection. Whirlwinds can also occur. The airflow sometimes rises and sometimes falls, without any certainty. At this time, the water vapor contained in the airflow cools or condenses into snow. When it descends, it may turn into water. When it rises again, it freezes into ice. In this way, rising and falling are uncertain, and the hail block increases in weight repeatedly. Finally, it reaches the ground. Small ones are like peas, large ones are like chicken eggs, and some are even larger. When hail falls to the ground, not only are livestock in the fields struck, but also crops are beaten, causing them to break and die prematurely. The area where hail falls may not be too wide, and the chance of hail falling is also very rare, so the damage is also relatively shallow.

The dew, frost, hail, and snow mentioned above, as well as clouds, fog, rain, and dew, are all transformed from water vapor. Water evaporates and becomes water vapor, which accumulates in the air. Water vapor condenses into clouds, fog, dew, frost, hail, snow, and rain due to the decrease in temperature. Among them, except for floating clouds, all fall back to the ground, either as sweet dew, severe frost, auspicious snow, or disastrous hail. And the rain that falls also has the distinction between timely rain and floodwater. Their impact on human life has different advantages and disadvantages, but they are all changes produced by water vapor. If there were no air on the ground and no changes in this water vapor, then all living things would not be able to exist. What we call meteorology is the specialized study of all the changes in wind, clouds, rain, and thunder in the atmosphere. If we want to know when there will be storms, when there will be sudden rains, when there will be frost, and when there will be hail, in order to ensure the safety of aviation, navigation, and agriculture, forestry, and killing animals, meteorological stations or observatories must be widely established in various places to make accurate forecasts based on precise records. Only in this way can we avoid mistakes. (The End)

Page 9

The transportation of goods is frequent, the market is prosperous, and they usually help each other and are in great need of each other. Recently, as soon as the banks in the city saw that the financial situation was tight, they stopped providing loans even more and earnestly pursued the repayment of loans that were due. With only inflows and no outflows, it has become exhausted. Various industries are showing signs of panic. As a result, businesses that have been forced to close down are emerging one after another. If we wait until the end of the year to close the accounts, in addition to the slightly original business numbers that may barely survive, all the others will have to cease operations. In order to maintain finance and relieve the market, we earnestly request that Your Excellency order the banks to provide loans as usual to maintain commerce, not to be unduly worried, and to take advantage of the difficulties of the people, only to seek personal gain and disregard public welfare. Then commerce will be fortunate, the region will be fortunate. In addition to submitting to the Department of Construction and sending a letter to the Department of Finance, we hereby submit a written request to Your Excellency for examination and approval and order immediate implementation. Respectfully presented by Chairman Han, Jinan Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Ma Duo, director of the Central Bank of this city, recently convened the city's financial community to explain the meaning of the currency reform and separately investigate the amount of foreign currency and types of banknotes held by various money exchanges and silver houses. However, since the suspension of silver, the number of chips in the market has suddenly felt tight. It has recently been heard that in order to provide emergency relief, the central government has allocated 300,000 yuan of legal tender. Ma Duo fears that this will still not be sufficient and has specially telegraphed the head office to allocate another 300,000 yuan of 1 yuan, 0.5 yuan, and 0.25 yuan legal tender. Mr. Ma originally planned to transfer a portion of the collected silver, about 200,000 to 300,000 yuan, to the central government for reminting into subsidiary currency. Later, fearing that this would have a negative impact on local finance, he has decided to stop the transfer. Mr. Ma also visited Governor Han Fuqu of the provincial government on the afternoon of the 11th to report on the progress of the handling. (November 11th)

Hubei Provincial Government Confirms Water Management Improvement Plan 81

Repairing Dikes Addresses the Symptoms, Dredging Addresses the Root Cause, Pursuing Both Separately. Central and Local Governments Divide Responsibilities for the Yangtze and Han Rivers.

Hankou Communication:

The Yangtze River Basin is a region of national wealth. The Han River flows through lands abundant in cotton and rice. Hubei, located between the Yangtze and Han Rivers, benefits from irrigation. However, in recent years, neglect of water management has led to frequent flooding. Over a decade ago, the Wangjiaying levee collapsed. Fifteen years ago, the Jianli Shiwan levee collapsed. The large-scale disasters of the twentieth year (of the Republic) and this year have caused particularly heavy losses to officials and civilians. The surging Yangtze and Han Rivers have almost become a source of calamity. The provincial government, learning from past mistakes, believes that addressing both the symptoms and root causes is necessary for lasting security. It has formulated eight improvement plans for water management, determined to implement them with maximum effort. The main points are summarized below:

(1) Reinforcing the Yangtze River Dikes in Hubei:

In water management, dredging is important for lowering the water channel, but reinforcing and securing the dikes remains crucial for flood prevention. After the Yangtze River dikes in Hubei were reinforced according to the flood level of the twentieth year, their height and thickness were considered adequate for protection. However, this year's water level exceeded the record of the twentieth year, causing many dikes in the upper reaches to be overtopped and breached. For safety, the dike tops must be raised by two meters, and the dike surface increased to sixty meters, with slope ratios of three and an average inner slope of one to six. Although this will be costly, failing to do so would entrust the livelihood of the nation to fate. The future danger is unimaginable.

(2) Dredging the Yangtze River:

The Yangtze River, flowing from Sichuan into Hubei, carries a strong current. It meanders between Yichang and Zhijiang, and receives the Ju and Zhang Rivers in Jingzhou, before merging with the Dongting Lake at Jinghe Nao, further increasing its momentum. Passing through Gong'an, Songzi, Shishou, and Jianli, the river course twists and turns, frequently becoming blocked. Its flow is lost into lakes, hindering regulation. This section of the Yangtze River is the most damaging to Hubei. Further downstream, places like Chenglingji, Baota Zhou, Jia Yu Gorge, and Ezhou Bay are particularly winding, impeding the water flow. Near Yangxia, it merges with the Han River, further increasing its volume. Flowing eastward, it is obstructed by the Qingshan and Xisai mountains, and constricted by Tianjiazhen, causing sediment buildup and the formation of sandbars. The accumulated floodwaters engulf Wuhan, causing a "fullness" and swelling. These are all causes of the water leaving its channel and flooding. Given the urgency of the current flood situation, dredging is imperative. In the Jinghe area, both the lake and river should be addressed, repairing the openings to the lake and restoring the original channel, using the lake's capacity to absorb the river and the river's flow to drain the lake. From Jianli to above Jinkou, river bends should be straightened to reduce meandering and turbulence. Therefore, effective methods should be adopted swiftly, sufficient funds raised, and both symptoms and root causes addressed, with dredging and repairs carried out simultaneously, to alleviate the suffering of our people.

(3) Managing the Xiang River:

The Xiang River originates in Shaanxi, flowing a thousand miles into Hubei. Similar to the Yangtze emerging from its gorges, it receives the waters of the Tang and Bai Rivers between Junzhou and Laohekou, further increasing its momentum. With flatlands on both banks, relying solely on levees to contain the river, frequent breaches and flooding cause great disasters. It is indeed a highly irregular riverbed. The plan is to block breaches, move back remote levees, and uniformly raise and reinforce all levee lines to prevent overflows. Meanwhile, upstream from Yunxi to above Xiangcheng, suitable terrain will be selected to build flood detention basins, forming reservoirs with the surrounding valleys. Alongside these, spillways will be constructed, allowing floodwaters to be temporarily stored. Only a safe flow rate will be allowed to gradually discharge from the spillways, achieving flow control. Between Zhongxiang Xiangkou Town and Dawang Temple, a diversion dam will be built, allowing high water levels to divert flow into the Tianmen River, through Diaowen Lake. The silted and shallow natural river channels will then be dredged, allowing the water to enter the Xiang River from X溝 (a new channel) and the Yangtze River from Chenjia Ji. This will reduce the flow of the Xiang River in the middle reaches and alleviate the threat to the northwest of Hankou. Furthermore, tributaries such as the Cekou River, Tongshun River, Niuti River, and Yejia River will be dredged in order of urgency. Large river bends along the river, such as Yangzikou in Hanchuan, will be straightened, allowing the water to flow through the land, ending the water woes of the people near the Han River.

(4) Planning for This Year's Construction:

After this year's floods, levee funds have been exhausted, and the people are destitute. Raising funds for both construction and relief is extremely difficult. It is imperative to make comprehensive plans where possible. The entire Xiang River and the silted and breached dikes of the upper Yangtze River have caused great suffering to the people. All levee repair projects should employ work-for-relief, using a lottery system to ensure benefits reach the people. Detailed plans have been formulated through consultation between the Jianghan Engineering Bureau and the General Relief Association for Water Disasters. As for the Yangtze River downstream from Xiy魚 (喜魚), except for Hanyang County, which suffered severe damage, most of the dikes and embankments (堤垸) remained intact. To compensate for the levee fund shortfall, it is proposed to conscript labor without pay to reinforce the main dikes, leveraging the power of the people to defend their own territory. The Jianghan Engineering Bureau should work with the General Relief Association for Water Disasters and the Department of Civil Affairs to thoroughly investigate areas not affected by the disaster but related to the dikes, and the number of able-bodied men in each area. They should also estimate the amount of earthwork, draw up charts, and assign sections to the heads of districts, *bao*, and *jia*, tasking them with conscripting laborers. The technical guidance will be provided by the engineering offices. The Tangzhuba dam project on the upper Xiang River should be contracted out. The dredging projects in the middle and lower reaches will be carried out as work-for-relief. Due to the difficulty in raising such large sums, it is proposed to use a military engineering accounting method to save costs and make the project easier to implement.

(5) Establishing Levee Management Agencies and Rationalizing the Division of Levee Section Jurisdiction:

The dikes of the Yangtze and Han Rivers in Hubei extend for thousands of miles, but the Jianghan Engineering Bureau has only established seven engineering offices to manage them. One office manages dike sections as long as five to six hundred *li*, requiring them to cross rivers and take care of both banks, handle annual repair projects, and face difficulty in supervision. During floods, dangerous situations arise frequently. More offices should be established where necessary to facilitate management. Long-distance telephones should be installed along the route to allow the conditions to be communicated at any time. The engineering offices will respond accordingly to avoid missed opportunities. The important river dikes should be managed by the Jianghan Engineering Bureau. However, due to the existing decisions from the levee work conference of the fifteenth year of the Republic, some Yangtze River dikes are excluded from the main dikes, such as the Jingjiang Dike in Jiangling and the Wuhui Dike in Wuchang. These should be included as main dikes under government repair to avoid mutual blame between officials and civilians during peacetime, and mutual avoidance during floods.

(6) Strengthening the Authority of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau and the Supervisory Guidance Power of the Provincial Government:

The Jianghan Engineering Bureau is directly subordinate to the National Economic Commission in terms of system. In reality, it should follow the orders of the Provincial Government, and the Bureau should have considerable freedom in making decisions. However, everything, regardless of urgency, must be reported to the NEC thousands of miles away. The annual repair projects, after long-term investigation by the engineering offices and review and design by the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, are often reduced by more than half by the NEC. This year, dike breaches occurred in many places where construction had been cut. As for the Provincial Government, it is not informed of the investigation and estimation, so it cannot exercise its guiding power, and it does not participate in the acceptance inspection, so it cannot fulfill its supervisory responsibility. In peacetime, official correspondence only creates unnecessary paperwork. The NEC should grant the Jianghan Engineering Bureau the power to select annual repair projects and allocate flood control funds and materials, without undue interference, to avoid delays. The Provincial Government bears the responsibility for the land and people of the province, so it must pay close attention to the dikes, which are closely related to the land and people, to ensure the appropriateness of the investigation and repair plan and the solidity of the repairs. The NEC must inform the Provincial Government to send personnel to jointly investigate and inspect to ensure the completion of its mission. The supervisory and guiding power during flood control should be completely entrusted to the Provincial Government for effective response. The NEC should only review the reimbursement afterward.

(7) Dividing and Organizing Water Conservancy Administration and Funding:

The Executive Yuan's outline for unified water conservancy administration and undertakings stipulates that water conservancy projects involving two or more provinces should be managed by the central water conservancy authority. The water conservancy administration of this province is already managed by the Jianghan Engineering Bureau established by the NEC, which mainly manages the Yangtze River, which seems to comply with the outline. However, in terms of managing the Han River, it should not belong to the central government. The NEC only handles dike funds in Hubei to manage dikes within Hubei and does not coordinate the water conservancy of the entire Yangtze River basin, which further undermines the meaning of the central agency managing local dikes. It is proposed to request that the NEC review the outline for unified water conservancy administration and take over the management of all Yangtze River water conservancy and dike projects to both reinforce the dikes and prevent current disasters and to raise large sums for fundamental dredging. The Xiang River only affects one province, so the local government should manage its dredging and repairs. As for the central government's Yangtze River management funds, there is much to be raised. Among the provinces along the Yangtze River, only Hubei has special dike funds. The sources of Hubei's dike funds are three types of surcharges: customs duties, special taxes, and land taxes, yielding about 1.2 million yuan annually. The customs duty surcharge accounts for 1.1 million. It is reasonable to levy Yangtze River construction donations from customs duties along the river. Hubei has been independently levying dike donations for the past decade, and the donation rate is quite high, but merchants are happy to pay. Yangtze River management should not be limited to Hubei, so the customs duty surcharge can be extended to the entire river. It is proposed that all customs offices from Chongqing to Shanghai levy a water conservancy donation at a rate of 5%, which would yield 10 million yuan annually, making any large-scale project feasible. The annual cost of Xiang River repair and defense is about 600,000 yuan, which is taken from the three types of surcharges for the Yangtze River dike project. It is now proposed that the central government universally levy donations from all customs offices along the river, and the Hubei customs duty surcharge will be abolished at the same time. The special tax revenue is decreasing due to the strict prohibition of opium, and it will disappear in a few years. Only the land tax surcharge remains, yielding about 100,000 yuan annually, which is insufficient to manage the Xiang River. It is proposed to request that the central government allocate one-tenth of the customs duty surcharge for a period of ten years to subsidize the province's Xiang River water storage, flood reduction, and other fundamental projects. The funds for reinforcing dikes and local dredging will be raised and managed, and conscripted labor will be used.

(8) Organizing and Managing Civilian Dikes:

Building dikes is the least desirable strategy for water management, and branch and civilian dikes often compete with water for land. In recent times, the lake surface has shrunk, and the river flow has narrowed, largely due to people building dikes to enclose silt. After the great flood of the twentieth year, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek proposed returning fields to the lake, which can be said to have identified the problem. However, not all dikes hinder the water flow, and people have long relied on them for survival, so they cannot be abolished without careful consideration. Hubei is located between the Yangtze and Han Rivers, with numerous tributaries and winding channels. The number of civilian dikes and their importance to national taxes and people's livelihood is comparable to the main dikes. Before a detailed water conservancy plan is comprehensively determined, they must be properly organized and reasonably regulated to avoid their harm and preserve their benefits. Civilian dikes are often low and thin, and those behind the main dikes often collapse first due to the pressure of the rising water in the inner rivers, then impacting the back of the main dikes. These should be investigated, and the beneficiary people should be ordered to reinforce them according to the height and slope of the main dikes.洲 (zhou - island) dikes outside the main dikes, except for those that excessively obstruct the water flow and must be abolished, are allowed to be repaired as before. For civilian dike repair projects, beneficiaries are assigned labor and fees based on acreage, and the government only supervises. However, after the flood, civilian dikes are mostly destroyed, and people are focused on saving lives, so assistance must be provided. The importance of the benefits and the financial strength of each area will be assessed, and subsidies or loans will be provided to help restore rural areas. (12th)

A Review of the Philippine Independence Movement (Part 2) 90

— Wu Hanfang

When President Wilson left office, he wrote a letter to Congress, saying: "Allow me to draw your attention to the fact that the political autonomy of the Filipinos is almost a success. For their benefit, and in accordance with what we have previously allowed them, it should be transformed from an ideal into a reality."

(6) The Special Committee's Investigation Report on the Philippines. After President Harding took office on March 4, 1921, he appointed a special committee, and former Governor General Wood and Cameron were sent to the Philippines to investigate all the circumstances and then make a report to the U.S. government, which would then use it as a basis to formulate a policy requiring American recognition and support. This special committee spent four months traveling throughout the Philippine islands and contacting the Filipino people extensively.

The report of this special committee has been published. Its contents are roughly the opinions of the U.S. President and the instructions to the special committee. There is also a brief history of the Philippines and the living conditions of the Filipinos. The more important part of this report is the analysis of the current situation in the Philippines. Now, in relation to the independence movement, a few paragraphs are quoted below:

We feel that the people of the Philippines are happy, peaceful, and value the benefits of American rule.

We feel that in every part of the Philippines, Filipinos who believe in Christianity hope for independence. Ordinary people under American protection, non-Christians, and Americans all hope that the United States will continue to govern.

We feel that if, after independence, it is still under the protection of another country, it is not true independence.

We feel that from the past eight years of experience, Filipinos have almost had a de facto autonomous government. If the United States abandons its political protection, withdraws its army and navy, and carelessly allows this island nation to be managed by the powers, while seeking the fertile land and various future commercial interests, then it can be said to be unjust. In short, if we withdraw from the Philippines and terminate our relationship with them without giving the Filipinos a good opportunity to establish an orderly and permanent autonomous government, then it would be a betrayal of the Filipinos, a misfortune for the Americans, blocking the path of Filipino progress and causing them to regress. Isn't such neglect of America's due obligations a very shameful matter?

We propose that the United States maintain the current state of the Philippines until they have full autonomy.

We propose that the United States have a responsible representative, the Governor-General of the Philippines, whose powers should be consistent with his position.

We propose that when a dispute arises between the Governor-General of the Philippines and the Philippine Senate regarding appointments that cannot be resolved, the U.S. President has the power to approve or reject and decide.

We propose that the U.S. government should not be willing to take responsibility for various undertakings on a certain island without actual power.

(7) Reasons Why the United States is Slow to Grant Independence to the Philippines. The reason why the Philippine independence movement has not been realized for a time is ultimately the conflict of practical interests. Further analysis reveals the following reasons:

First, reasons of national defense. The future situation in the Pacific is becoming increasingly perilous. Japan is naturally a thorn in the side of the United States. Furthermore, the Netherlands has the East Indies, France has Indochina, and Britain has Hong Kong, Singapore, and the Malay Peninsula, all of which have a deep foundation in military and commercial terms. If the United States does not have a Philippines as its naval base, then it will not be able to maintain the balance of power in the Far East, and the United States' great commerce in the Far East will be in some danger. The British naval admiral stationed in Hong Kong once said, "If the American flag is lowered in Manila, the British flag will be raised in its place." Americans also often say, "If the Americans withdraw from the Philippines in the morning, the Japanese will enter in the evening." This is because the United States is very wary of the powers surrounding the Philippines. This is the reason why the United States is unwilling to easily give up the Philippines and quickly grant the Philippines independence due to national defense concerns.

Second, economic reasons. Since 1909, free trade has been practiced between the United States and the Philippines. The United States, as the suzerain power, has annual trade worth 100 million yuan to the Philippines. If a 20% tariff were levied, 20 million yuan could be saved. Furthermore, every year, the Philippines imports wheat produced from 200,000 acres, cotton produced from 100,000 acres, and apples from 3,150 acres of orchards, with cars worth over 1 million yuan. If the Philippines becomes an independent country, then both countries will lose the benefits of free trade. Other countries, with low labor costs, will sell tobacco, sugar, hemp, and coconut oil to the U.S. market, and of course they will be able to win. There will naturally be many obstacles to the import of American products into the Philippines. Moreover, the Philippines owes the United States a total of 70 million gold yuan, and the United States has invested 20 million yuan in the Philippines. They believe that once they leave the Philippines, they will inevitably suffer a loss of 100 million yuan. Therefore, from an economic perspective, the United States is also unwilling to easily grant the Philippines independence for a time.

(8) The Success of the Independence Movement. Since the Philippine independence movement began in 1907, they have continued to struggle unceasingly. In recent years, the Filipinos have been influenced by the doctrine of national self-determination, and coupled with the ardent national patriotism, the independence movement has reached a mature stage. Independence movement leaders such as current President Quezon and Senator Osmeña are the most enthusiastic. They have successively gone to the United States, using peaceful methods and a sincere attitude, to make strong requests to the U.S. authorities and people. In fact, the achievements of the United States' rule over the Philippines for more than 30 years have been evident to the world. Although it cannot be separated from being an imperialist, the policy it has adopted is generous, with no territorial ambitions, and has a style of encouraging and supporting small and weak nations. This is beyond the reach of the selfish and self-interested colonial policies of various countries on the European continent. In all fairness, since the Americans ruled the Philippines, their management of the Filipinos has been extremely free, never as harsh as the Dutch and British treat their colonies. Moreover, the number of American administrative personnel stationed in the Philippines has been gradually reduced year by year. When the author visited the Philippines five years ago and observed its various government agencies, the number of American officials was almost zero, which shows their attitude towards the Philippines. The United States granting independence to the Philippines was originally a matter of time. However, when the internal strength of the Philippines was not sufficient, the United States, due to national defense issues and economic reasons, was not in a good position to abandon it immediately. This year, both the U.S. Senate and House of Representatives have passed the Philippine Independence Act, allowing it to establish an autonomous government immediately, with the United States responsible for maintaining the independence of the Philippines for ten years. The reason why there is such a satisfactory solution is that the various reciprocal conditions for free trade and commerce between the United States and the Philippines still exist, so economics is no longer a problem. The U.S. Army, Navy, and Air Force are still stationed in the Philippines, ostensibly to deal with the situation in the Pacific, but in reality, they still regard themselves as protectors of the Philippines. Moreover, the U.S. promise to grant independence to the Philippines should not be repeatedly given verbally but not actually delivered. Therefore, the Philippine independence movement of more than 30 years can be said to be completely successful today.

The Philippine autonomous government has already been established, and the first president, Quezon, has also been elected. On November 15th of this year, a grand celebration was held to mark the official establishment of the new Philippine government. The United States specially sent U.S. Vice President Garner and Army Chief of Staff Bourne, among other important figures, to participate. This move is indeed sufficient to express the friendship between the peoples and governments of the United States and the Philippines. However, on the other hand, this invitation has a profound intention. The Philippine government and people hope that they will get to know the administrative and legislative personnel who will reform Philippine affairs in the new government, and be able to understand the administration of the new government personnel in the Far East and on the island, and the result will be that the new government personnel will have convenience in future legislation. From this, it can be seen that the cooperation and friendship between the United States and the Philippines continue to exist.

The Filipinos have raised the banner of independence high, establishing a brand new independent and national state in Asia. Its position in the international community will be on par with the independent countries of China, Japan, and the Philippines. Furthermore, the relationship between China and the Philippines is particularly close. We have more than 200,000 overseas Chinese residing in the Philippines, who hold a leading position in the economy. Moreover, China and the Philippines have a long history of relationship, with intermarriage and ethnic groups being extremely close. From now on, we come to celebrate the success of the Philippine independence movement and the genuine friendship, co-existence, and co-prosperity of China and the Philippines in the future.

Ministry of Finance Orders the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Sincerely Convey the Central Government's Intentions; the Central Government's Assignment to the Three Banks to Stabilize Foreign Exchange Has Been Effective 91

The Ministry of Finance issued a public notice stating that after the banknotes of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications became legal tender, the entire country would comply, strictly prohibiting the private transportation of silver and the raising of prices, and ordering the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to sincerely convey the central government's intentions. The three banks have stabilized foreign exchange and have achieved results. The details are recorded as follows:

Ministry Order Conveying the Central Government's Intentions

The Ministry of Finance approved Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Document No. Qian Zi 7808, stating: "The telegram has been received. The stabilization of prices has already been telegraphed to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering them to handle it conscientiously. If there are those who seek to speculate and raise prices, they should be punished according to the law without any leniency. As for stabilizing foreign exchange prices, the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications should be responsible, and the Ministry has issued orders to the relevant banks to observe the market conditions at any time and assist in handling them. Now, at the time when the unified issuance and centralized reserve measures have just been implemented, a small number of people may not yet understand. The Chamber of Commerce is still requested to sincerely convey the intentions of the Central Government, so as to stabilize the market, stabilize people's minds, and lead the country to prosperity. This is of utmost importance. This order."

Strictly Prohibit Private Transportation and Raising Prices

The Ministry of Finance has already ordered all customs offices to strictly investigate the private transportation of silver, and has at the same time consulted the provincial and municipal governments to assist. It is now heard that a small number of cigarette shops and small money houses are buying silver, with the aim of seeking small profits. After receiving the report, they will immediately pay close attention and severely punish the investment merchants who buy silver. As for stabilizing prices, the provincial and municipal governments have already been telegraphed to handle it conscientiously. If there are those who seek to speculate and raise prices, they should be punished according to the law without any leniency. As for the four items previously determined by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to prohibit the raising of prices, they have already been approved for filing by the Municipal Government.

Stabilizing Foreign Exchange Has Been Effective

Regarding the case of stabilizing foreign exchange prices, the Ministry of Finance issued orders to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to observe the market conditions at any time and cooperate in handling them. Now, Xi Demao, Director of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank, Bei Songsun, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, and Zhang Peishen, Manager of the Business Bureau of the Bank of Communications, meet every day at 10:00 a.m. in the Foreign Exchange Department of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank to discuss stabilizing prices, without restricting the buying and selling of foreign exchange. This has been effective, and the prices have been very stable in recent days. Yesterday, the prices announced by the Central Bank for foreign exchange of five countries, including the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, France, and Japan, were the same as the day before. As for the equalization tax rate, it is still 57.25%.

Currency Exchange Rates Have Become Stable

Yesterday, the money market saw single and double jiao coins at 833 yuan and 3 jiao. Copper coins were at 300,000 per thousand, exchangeable for 1,200 jiao. Cloth tokens were at 3,000 wen, jiao blanks at 250 wen, and interest at 50 wen. However, the various cigarette shops saw a surge in exchange rates due to the large amount of copper coins sold by the public bus company and the tram company, with each yuan exchangeable for 10 jiao and 480 wen, up to 12 jiao and 10 wen, and copper coins at 2,960 wen to 3,150 wen. Double hao coins were at 490 wen to 510 wen, which is already equal to the standard of auxiliary coin prices stipulated by the Ministry of Finance.

After the Ministry of Finance implemented the new monetary policy, there have been instances of excessive price increases in the city. According to a report from the Central News Agency reporter to the person in charge of the bureau, after the bureau was ordered to suppress excessive price increases, it immediately began to investigate the costs of various commodities. The interests of the industrial and commercial sectors should naturally be taken into account, and the purchasing power of general employers should also be considered at the same time. Prices will be stipulated under these two principles. Now, the industrial and commercial sectors can comply with the bureau's investigation of costs and stipulation of prices. Among them, there are those who need foreign raw materials and other imported goods, and the prices are higher due to exchange rate reasons. This phenomenon does not harm the national industry and commerce, and may even be beneficial. However, for export commodities, due to the decrease in the price of silver, they will gradually increase in the future. The Municipal Public Security Bureau Re-Investigates the City's Household Registration, Issuing Forms on the 16th and Collecting Them on the 19th 96

Cai Jingjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, considering that the city's household registration is not very detailed and complete, specially obtained approval from the Municipal Government to allocate funds to conduct a special large-scale investigation to improve it. He has repeatedly convened meetings at the bureau with the directors and staff members of the subordinate branch bureaus, household registration patrol officers, etc., and decided to organize an investigation team, promoting Hong Qi, the chief of the Second Section, as the team leader, and Li Zemin, the director of household registration, as the deputy team leader. The staff members of the branch bureaus are the company commanders, the household registration patrol officers are the platoon leaders, the police chiefs are the group leaders, and the police officers are the group members. There are a total of about 1,800 staff members, all wearing white cloth armbands with "Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Household Registration Investigation" printed on them. They have also printed notices and household registration forms, and it is scheduled that on the 16th of this month, the team leader will lead the departure, investigating and persuading door-to-door, and distributing a notice and a household registration form to each household, requiring them to fill in the number of men, women, and children truthfully, and to complete and submit the forms by the 19th, without hiding or omitting anything. If they are unable to write, the police officers will write on their behalf, and they will be required to complete the procedures and report them by the end of this month. It is also heard that the purpose of this special investigation of household registration is: (1) to clarify the city's population, (2) to accurately know whether there are any omissions in the number of opium smokers, (3) to determine the effectiveness of the literacy movement among the people of this city. After this investigation, the household registration procedures of each branch bureau will also be reformed. In the past, the triangular sign used for household registration mainly used the street name and house number. Now, because this sign is not very agile during inspection, it will be changed to a card book cover, with the name as the standard. It will be more convenient to check the population when needed than the street name and house number.

Raw Silk Exports Are Active; More Than 20,000 Bales Shipped Out in Five Months; Miao Zhongxiu Discusses Two Important Reasons 99

According to the Guomin News Agency, the export of raw silk from this city has been particularly active this year. From June to the end of October, in five months, it has reached 33,562 bales. Among the raw silk exported, the most was shipped to the United States, totaling 15,055 bales, followed by Europe, totaling 13,261 bales. The least was shipped to Asia and Africa. According to Miao Zhongxiu, Director of the Silk Inspection Group of the Commodity Inspection Bureau, the reasons for the sudden increase in raw silk exports this year are: first, the increase in silk production overseas, such as the success of the United States' recovery and France; the second important reason is the reduction in Japan's raw silk production this year.

Chamber of Commerce Letter Replying to Jiangwan Office: Instructing Agencies for Exchanging Legal Tender 107

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce received a letter yesterday from its Jiangwan branch office stating that there were no exchange agencies for the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, or the Bank of Communications in the district. They proposed that the Chamber of Commerce forward a request to the municipal government to designate the Land Tax Collection Office and the post office as agencies for exchanging legal tender for convenience. The Chamber of Commerce immediately replied, stating that on the 6th of this month, they received Order No. 56 from the Shanghai Monetary Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance. The order stated that in remote areas where the banknotes of the three banks were not yet widely circulated, those holding silver coins or silver should be able to exchange them for legal tender. Therefore, the Ministry had ordered the three banks, all banks and money shops, all public associations, all tax collection agencies, and all state-run enterprises (such as postal, telegraph, railway, and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company bureaus) to act as exchange agents. The Chamber of Commerce had already notified all public associations, member merchants, and branch offices of this order on November 7. The Jiangwan office could simply notify the merchants in its jurisdiction to exchange silver coins or silver for legal tender at the Land Tax Collection Office and the post office without needing to forward a request for specific designation.

Hankou Newspaper Exhibition Seeking Submissions 108

Various organizations in Hankou have scheduled a National Newspaper and Magazine Exhibition for New Year's Day next year. They have specially sent Lin Rongkui, director of the Propaganda Department of the Hankou Municipal Party Headquarters, to Shanghai to solicit exhibits. He has already contacted various newspaper offices and bookstores in the city and made preliminary arrangements. He has also traveled to Hangzhou to carry out various aspects of the plan. To facilitate submissions, Lin has arranged for the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters to be responsible for collecting exhibits. Furthermore, all shipping costs for exhibits sent directly to Hankou will be borne by Hankou. All items returned will be delivered one week after the close of the exhibition without delay. Fudan University and the Hangzhou Journalists' Association have both agreed to lend all the news materials they have collected over the years to support the event. Lin is scheduled to return to Shanghai from Hangzhou within days to ship a portion of the exhibits westward. The submission guidelines are as follows:

甲. Newspapers:

(1) Inaugural issues, anniversary issues, special issues, and recently published issues.

(2) Newspapers published for more than ten years that have undergone reforms; the issues before and after the reforms are also requested.

(3) Newspapers published in foreign languages but run by Chinese.

(4) Newspapers run by overseas Chinese in various locations.

(5) Newspapers that have ceased publication but have historical revolutionary value.

乙. Magazines and Pictorials:

(1) Inaugural issues, anniversary issues, special issues, and recently published issues.

(2) Magazines published for more than five years that have undergone reforms; all reformed issues are also requested.

(3) For magazines that have ceased publication, the earliest and latest issues are requested.

(4) Same as Items 3, 4, and 5 for newspapers.

丙. Gazettes:

(1) Regular and irregular publications of the central and local governments.

(2) Except for publications for temporary special events, all are requested. For publications of the same nature issued continuously, the earliest and latest issues are requested.

丁. Children's Reading Materials:

(1) All children's reading materials published by various organizations, groups, schools, and bookstores nationwide are requested as much as possible.

(2) Reference the submission guidelines for newspapers.

Notes:

(1) All publications listed above for submission must not be those prohibited by the central government.

(2) Receiving address: Hankou Special Municipality Party Headquarters.

(3) Shanghai temporary receiving address: Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters.

Third Anniversary of the Death of Yu Zongzhou, Founder of the Chinese Christian Self-Governing Church 113

Christianity was introduced to our country from the West more than a century ago. The number of believers and the scale of the work are well known to the Chinese people. However, because all the work and financial resources were completely dependent on friendly foreign people, thirty years ago, Presbyterian pastor Yu Zongzhou believed it was a great shame for the Chinese people. He resolutely initiated a self-governing church, named the Chinese Christian Self-Governing Church in Shanghai. Soon, the whole country responded and established self-governing churches. He achieved great success. This year, November 17, marks the third anniversary of Yu's death. Yu passed away at the age of eighty. It is reported that the National General Council of the church has scheduled a memorial service for Yu Zongzhou this Sunday afternoon at 2:00 PM at the General Church on Xiangyin Road.

Priority Payment of Employees' Debts: Trade Unions in the Hotel Industry and Others Telegraph Request for Clear Enforcement 114

The Shanghai Automobile Drivers' Trade Union, the Hotel Industry Trade Union, and others sent a telegram to the Fifth Plenary Session requesting that employees' debts should enjoy the highest priority of repayment. The telegram read: "To all members and representatives of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang, the congress is grandly opened, and the people are joyful. At this time of national crisis and hardship for the people, we rely on your planning and decision-making to reverse the tide. Our trade union has read the suggestion made by lawyer Zhou Lianze, a member of the Chinese Labor Association, to your congress, regarding 'Priority Payment of Employees' Debts.' We endorse this proposal sincerely as it relates to the interests of all members of our trade union. Since unified laws and regulations have not been formulated, most employees have no basis for claiming priority payment of their debts, and they may starve. The nature of employees' debts is different from the nature of other debts, and they should not be compared. For example, drivers' and workers' guarantee deposits, and hotel waiters' and servants' deposits, are not clearly regulated in national legislation, and they are greatly affected by the lack of legal protection. We hope that all members and representatives of the congress will consider the late Premier's intention to protect labor and the hardships of the working masses. Please approve the suggestion, submit it to the Legislative Yuan for amendment, and clearly enforce it. Then, the workers of the whole country will be blessed, and the nation and the people will be fortunate." Signed, Shanghai Hotel Industry Trade Union, Shanghai Taxi Drivers' Trade Union.

Public Concession: Industrial Accident Report for October 116

The Shanghai Municipal Council reports that there were a total of 150 accidental events in the factories of the Public Concession in October. Compared with the total number of over 200 incidents in the first half of this year, it seems that there has been much progress. However, it is still difficult to determine whether the actual number of accidents has decreased sharply, because the reporting may not be ideal or widespread enough. Furthermore, this matter is related to the economic depression in Shanghai. If factories are closed or reduce production, the number of accidents will naturally decrease accordingly. Among the above accidents, six people died, and two women were injured. Classified by industry, the highest number of accidents still occurred in the machinery and hardware industry, with a total of 48 incidents, but no deaths. The construction industry reported 16 incidents, with 2 deaths. The textile industry reported 14 incidents, with 2 deaths. The food and beverage manufacturing industry reported 8 incidents, with 1 death. The transportation industry reported 9 incidents, with 1 death. As for the causes, among the six deaths, five were due to falls from heights, and 30 people were injured by falls. The remaining death was due to burns.

Flying Girl Brand Cigarettes: Verification of Stamp Authenticity 117

All brands of cigarettes produced by the Luxin Tobacco Factory at No. 19 Rue Paul Beau in the French Concession are distributed and sold wholesale by the Yixin Distributor at No. 549 Avenue Joffre. On the afternoon of the 5th of this month, inspectors Zhou Baosheng, Zhu Qiming, Zhao Chengen, and others from the Shanghai French Concession Cigarette Inspection Office of the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance inspected the Yixin Distributor. They found that the stamps of the Shanghai Cigarette Inspection Office and the Nanshi Inspection Office on the wrappers of 29 boxes of Flying Girl brand cigarettes produced by the Luxin Tobacco Factory (500 cigarettes per box, totaling 14,500 cigarettes) were inconsistent. The original stamp was suspected of being counterfeited. On February 1, February 18, and July 31 of this year, markings had been made on the lines printed on the stamp. It was believed that the Luxin factory owner, Yu Luxin (35 years old, from Shandong), had counterfeited the stamps to evade taxes. Yu Luxin was arrested and sent to the Special No. 2 Court for investigation and detention on the afternoon of that day. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the criminal court judge interrogated him in the Criminal Division No. 1. A lawyer representing the Cigarette Inspection Office stated that the Police Department had not yet completed the investigation procedures for identifying the stamps of the Inspection Office and requested a postponement. The defendant denied the forgery and hired a lawyer to defend him. The court ordered a postponement to the 19th for further interrogation, and the defendant was returned to custody.

Qiu Feihai: Settlement in Case of Girl Crushed to Death by Car 129

Qiu Feihai, a tennis player from Xiamen, drove his friend's car No. 6474 at around 6:00 AM on July 30 of this year, passing Foch Road in the French Concession. Due to the driver's negligence, he hit and killed the ten-year-old daughter of Huang Hanting, from Jiangxi, who lived at No. 29 Ci Hou North Li, Ha Tong Road. Lawyers Fan Gang and Huang Xuanzhang filed a criminal lawsuit and an attached civil suit in the Special No. 2 Court against Qiu, requesting damages of 11,400 yuan. Qiu also hired a lawyer to defend him. The trial concluded, finding that Qiu was indeed negligent and sentenced him to a fine of 300 yuan and damages of 2,000 yuan to the plaintiff. Qiu, dissatisfied with the judgment, appealed to the Senior Third Branch Court. The plaintiff, Huang Hanting, believing that the original sentence was too light and that the attached civil suit was insufficient, also appealed to the Senior Third Branch Court. The High Court, upon receiving the complaint, held a hearing yesterday, presided over by acting Presiding Judge Sun Honglin, accompanied by judges and prosecutors. Both appellants were represented by lawyers. Lawyer Fan Gang stated that the plaintiff had also filed an appeal, but both parties had reached an out-of-court settlement. Because the procedures had not yet been completed, he requested a three-day extension to allow the settlement to be finalized and the appeal to be withdrawn. Chen Zhongyin, the lawyer, stated that the appellant, Qiu Feihai, had gone to Singapore and was not in Shanghai. A friend was acting on his behalf to reach a settlement, but the withdrawal of the appeal had to be sent to Singapore for Qiu to sign himself and returned for submission. The mailing would take two weeks. The court approved both parties' requests for a postponement. It is reported that for the civil part of the case, Qiu will pay 1,900 yuan, settling the case.
