Guanyin Salvation Association Preparatory Meeting 132

Distributing the "Guanyin Salvation Collection," Seeking Founders

The Shanghai Guanyin Salvation Association (at the intersection of Baylor Road and Avenue Joffre) was initiated by layman Chen Weixin of Songjiang, with enthusiastic support from believers in Guanyin from all quarters. A preparatory meeting was held yesterday at 3:00 PM, during which officers for various departments were elected. Over thirty preparatory committee members attended, chaired by layman Chen Weixin. He reported on the association's founding process, stating that he had been blessed by Buddha in previous lives, escaping disasters and suffering. He himself had suffered from an eye ailment, losing his sight and nearly losing his life, but was protected by the Bodhisattva and regained his health. Out of gratitude for the Bodhisattva's profound kindness, he had taken refuge in the Three Jewels ten years prior and vowed to uphold six vows: 1. To promote the Buddha, Dharma, and Sangha; 2. To repent for the sins of body, speech, and mind; 3. To broadly relieve the suffering of all beings; 4. To universally encourage reciting the Buddha's name and releasing living creatures; 5. To advocate for a Buddhist utopian society; 6. To vow to ascend to the Pure Land together. He hoped that all members of the association would embody the Bodhisattva's great compassion and work to alleviate suffering, eliminate calamities, and pray for peace. Subsequently, officers for various departments were elected, and all officers took their oaths of office. Next, the charter of the preparatory office was approved. Layman Chen Dingyi then explained the procedures for soliciting founders and members. Finally, preparatory members gave free speeches, and the meeting adjourned after refreshments. The "Guanyin Salvation Collection," edited by Mr. Chen, has been published. The contents include exquisitely printed images of the Bodhisattva, the Panchen Lama, Wang Yiting, Huang Qinglan, inscriptions by prominent laymen, sacred sites of the Bodhisattva, sutras, Dharma sayings, records of releasing living creatures, stories of inspiration, and more. The last part includes the Guanyin Salvation Association's constitution, totaling over eighty pages and over one hundred thousand words. If every household has a copy, it can serve as a guide for the public to return to the right path and believe in Guanyin Bodhisattva. The association is currently distributing the collection free of charge in person. For mail requests, please include a five-cent postage stamp for delivery.

Wang Liunian Dies from Alcohol-Related Injuries 140

Wang Liunian, a 26-year-old man from Yancheng, made a living pulling a rickshaw in Shanghai. He lived in a shed owned by Wang Wanxiao, a fellow villager, at No. 133 Nanjin Road in the French Concession. Wang was a young man with a strong personality and enjoyed competing. On the afternoon of the 13th, at 3:00 PM, after finishing his shift and returning to his residence, he and his fellow villagers used salted vegetables and braised beef as appetizers and drank. After drinking, he became heavily intoxicated and lay down on the bed, unconscious. At 5:00 PM in the evening, he became delirious, feeling severe abdominal pain and restlessness. People in the residence thought he had contracted an epidemic and took him to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road. The doctor found that he was suffering from excessive alcohol consumption and performed a stomach lavage, removing a significant amount of alcohol and beef residue. He became conscious and was carried back to his residence to sleep at 8:00 PM. At 6:30 AM yesterday morning, he died from internal injuries. The owner of the residence, Wang Wanxiao, reported the incident to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall autopsy center, awaiting an autopsy by a representative from the Second Special Court today.

Exchange Industry Convenes Meeting to Discuss Supporting the Legal Tender 142

Notifying Fellow Traders to Prevent the Outflow of Silver Dollars; Rectifying Exchange Rates to Ensure Citywide Uniformity

The Shanghai Exchange Industry Association received letters from various branch offices stating that, although copper coin exchange rates have been set in recent days, market fluctuations have been inconsistent. For example, on the day before yesterday (the 13th), the market rate reached 3,150 wen per dollar, causing significant losses for traders. Those unfamiliar with the situation accused the exchange industry of manipulating prices. In reality, the exchange industry exchanges silver and copper coins based on money market rates, earning only a small profit. On the afternoon of the 13th, an emergency meeting of executive and supervisory committee members and branch office directors and deputy directors was convened. Attendees included Shen Weiting, Chen Liangyu, Chen Ruilin, Xian Wenda, Mi Chuxin, Teng Zhixiang, Chen Zaiyue, and over twenty others. Chairman Shen Weiting reported on the situation and the need to prevent the outflow of silver dollars, as well as the need to rectify copper coin exchange rates. Chen Liangyu expressed his opinions, and after discussion, the following measures were decided: (1) Notify all traders that if they have silver dollars, they should exchange them for legal tender at the designated three banks to comply with the law and avoid private trading or hoarding for profit. (2) Regarding the exchange rates for silver and copper coins, a uniform method will be formulated and representatives will be sent to negotiate with relevant parties before further discussion. Other cases were also discussed. The meeting adjourned late in the evening. The notice is excerpted below: Notice: Previously, the government issued an order that all silver coins (i.e., silver dollars) would be discontinued from November 4th and must be exchanged for legal tender at the "Central," "China," and "Communications" Banks. This association has unanimously supported this policy. However, all traders who have silver dollars in stock or who have accumulated them through exchange should promptly exchange them for legal tender at the designated three banks to comply with the law and avoid private trading or hoarding for profit, which would be illegal. All traders are urged to pay attention and avoid mistakes.

Astronomer Discusses Reason for Consecutive Days of Gloomy Weather: Rain in Changsha and Nanchang, Low Pressure Passing East over Shanghai 143

According to the Central News Agency, the consecutive days of gloomy weather, with the sky threatening rain but not actually raining, and the warm climate, which is unusual for early winter, has surprised many people. However, according to an astronomer, this weather is due to rain in the Changsha and Nanchang areas of Central China, and low pressure passing east over Shanghai. However, this low pressure is not considered excessively low. If the upper reaches of the Yangtze River clear up, or if the low pressure from Siberia moves south, the weather in the city will become clear and the climate will turn cold. Yesterday, the highest temperature before 3:30 PM was 66.2 degrees, and the lowest was 59.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 63.3 degrees and the lowest was 41.9 degrees. This year's temperature is warmer than last year.

Rickshaw Carts Not Subject to Quantity Restrictions 145

At a board meeting of the Public Concession Bureau the day before yesterday, the issue of rickshaw carts was discussed in detail. It was generally agreed that the management of these heavy-load vehicles, which are pushed and pulled by manpower, involves two major considerations: first, whether the operation of these vehicles obstructs traffic; and second, what impact they have on the smoothness of the road surface. These issues had been discussed in detail by various departments of the Public Concession Bureau and submitted to the Police Preparedness Committee for review. The two departments most closely related to this matter are the Engineering Department and the Police Department. The Engineering Department proposed that, in order to maintain the smoothness of the road surface, these vehicles should be equipped with certain types of wheels. The Police Department proposed that the number of vehicles should be restricted and that rickshaw carts should not be allowed to operate on certain roads. After discussion, the Police Preparedness Committee stated that, regarding the obstruction of traffic, the number of these manpower-pushed cargo vehicles has been increasing since 1925. If this trend is not curbed, road congestion is inevitable and should be restricted. However, one commissioner opposed this view, stating that restricting the number of vehicles would create a monopoly. The license fee should be used as a tool to manage the number of vehicles so that the current number does not continue to increase indefinitely. After detailed discussion, it was decided to recommend to the board of directors: (1) Do not restrict the number of vehicle licenses; (2) Add the following regulations to the Road Regulations: "The following locations are prohibited: Renmin Road, North Sichuan Road, Bazilu Road south of Sichuan Road, Sichuan Road, Waibaidu Bridge, etc."; (3) From July 1st next year, these vehicles must be equipped with 3.5-inch solid angle iron wheels or 2-inch solid rubber tires; (4) There will be no rewards or penalties for the installation of the above-mentioned wheels and tires; (5) The existing regulations on the number of loads will not be changed for the time being. It is reported that the above-mentioned measures have been accepted and implemented by the board of directors.

Young Man and Woman Jump into the River, One Dies, One Survives 146

Zhou Didi Forcibly Pulled Her to Her Death, Zhao Juhong Said

At 11:15 PM the night before last, a young man and woman suddenly arrived at the Guangxing Road pier in Yangshupu and hired sampan boat No. 624, driven by Ge Zhipin, to cross the river, stating that they wanted to go to the Hefeng Factory pier in Pudong. The man and woman boarded the boat hand in hand, behaving intimately. Unexpectedly, when they reached the middle of the river (next to buoy No. 25), the man and woman jumped into the river to commit suicide. Ge Zhipin was shocked and quickly stopped rowing and tried to rescue them. He managed to pull the woman up, who was fortunate to survive, but the man disappeared, presumably joining the water spirits. Ge Zhipin then took the woman to the water patrol police station. According to the report, after the man and woman got on the boat, I intended to lower the awning to avoid the wind and rain because it was raining, but the male passenger blocked me, saying that it was not necessary to lower it and urged me to row quickly. When we were about halfway across the river, the man and woman stood up, and I vaguely saw the male passenger push the female passenger to stand on the flat baseboard at the bow of the boat. The female passenger seemed unwilling. Unexpectedly, the female passenger stepped onto the flat baseboard with her left foot, and the male passenger fell into the river from the middle of the boat, dragging the female passenger down with him. I saw this and immediately tried to rescue them, only managing to rescue the female passenger. The male passenger had already disappeared. The police chief questioned the woman, who stated that her name was Zhao Juhong, 19 years old, from Changzhou, and lived at No. 187 Huaxingfang, Yangshupu. She had parents at home and had been betrothed to someone, but had not yet married. She left home tonight to chat with her sisters. When she walked to Shunxing Street, Yangshupu, she met a man surnamed Mou, who worked as a clerk in a yarn factory. He asked me if I was working, and I replied that I wasn't, but I had been beaten and insulted by his wife, so I was reasoning with him. Because it was raining, we went to the pier to avoid the rain. Later, he called for a sampan boat to cross the river, and he forced me to jump into the river. I didn't want to, but I was eventually dragged down. Fortunately, I was rescued. The police chief believed that the woman was still unwilling to reveal the man's name, so it was impossible to investigate thoroughly. However, the deceased's residence was presumably not far away. He then ordered Detective Liang Shenqing to find out that the deceased's name was Zhou Didi, 25 years old, from Shanghai, who worked in the electricity room of the Tongxing Yarn Factory in Yangshupu. He lived in the factory's workshop at No. 119 Shunxing Street. Detective Liang then summoned the deceased's wife, Zhou Li (23 years old, from Yancheng), and Zhao Juhong's mother, Zhao Xuan, to the police station. Yesterday afternoon, he prepared a document and ordered Detective Liang to transfer Zhao Juhong, along with sampan boat owner Ge Zhipin, Zhou Li, Zhao Xuan, and others, to the prosecutor's office of the local court for review.

Testimony of Hao Zhongyang in the Case of the Strange Female Corpse 147

Qiao Qishi Claims She Does Not Recognize the Witness; Judge Schedules On-Site Investigation Today

At 2:00 PM on August 3rd of this year, when the Beiyang-class Shengjing steamship docked at Pier No. 3 of Taikoo Dock in the French Concession was departing, the turning propeller stirred up a strange female corpse in the river. At that time, Maiwoman Zhang Zhou identified the corpse as her niece, Zhang Jinlin (48 years old). Her lower body was unclothed, indicating that she had been murdered. The court dispatched police to arrest a woman named Qiao Qishi. After clear interrogation by Prosecutor Xie Lian, the defendant Qiao Qishi was charged with Article 271, Section 1 of the Criminal Law for joint murder, although she refused to confess to the joint killing. However, according to witness testimony, the details were vivid. The criminal court had previously held a public trial that was not concluded. Details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. At 11:00 AM yesterday, Judge Yang Xiangzu specially opened the Thirteenth Court to continue the trial. The defendant Qiao Qishi hired attorney Fang Junjie to appear in court to defend her. After the judge took the bench, he first brought the imprisoned Qiao Qishi and the plaintiff Zhang Zhou to the case and questioned them briefly. Then, he summoned witness Hao Zhongyang to the stand. He stated that he was 30 years old, from Haimen, residing at No. 9 Diandang Lane, Pudong, and worked as a dock laborer. At around 10:00 PM on August 2nd of this year, I was enjoying the cool air on the Taikoo Dock and saw a yellow car parked there. Two men, three women, and a child were sitting in it. After getting out of the car, the two men walked in front, with the deceased and her (pointing to Qiao Qishi) walking behind. Later, they sat on the dockside eating watermelon seeds (sitting around talking and laughing). I didn't think much of it. Later, I saw a man take off the deceased's pants. I guessed they were doing something improper. I thought it was bad luck and went to sleep. About 1:45 later, I suddenly heard a splash in the river and realized that they had pushed a woman into the river. I wanted to help, but a man with a black mole on his face and a dragon tattoo on his arm slapped me once and punched me twice. I fell to the ground. When I got up, they had all run away. When the corpse was found the next day, I said that the corpse was murdered and thrown into the river last night, so I was called to be a witness. Questioned by the judge, Qiao Qishi claimed that she rarely went out and did not recognize the witness, claiming she had been framed. She asked for leniency. The judge considered that the circumstances of the case were serious and required further on-site investigation. He scheduled to personally visit the Taikoo Dock to conduct an investigation at 9:00 AM the next day (today) and instructed the witness to come to the court at that time and demonstrate what happened at the scene. The witness complied with the order. The judge then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Wang Changlin Accused by Adoptive Mother 148

Lawsuit over Mother-Son Identity; Official Urges Out-of-Court Settlement

Madam Wang Shi, a resident, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special Court against her adopted son, Wang Changlin, currently a staff member of a certain bank, to confirm their mother-son relationship, request payment of alimony, and recover past debts. She detailed that when the defendant was young, she nurtured him, intentionally cultivating him during his school years, and even took care of the clothing and food of his biological mother and sisters, with the money spent being difficult to quantify. Consequently, her husband's inheritance was almost entirely used up. Originally, she hoped that the defendant would return after completing his studies, and they could rely on each other as mother and son. Unexpectedly, after he gained social status and became an assistant manager at a bank, with a rich monthly income, he became wealthy and his attitude changed drastically, abandoning her and indifferently watching his over sixty-year-old mother, whose life was like a flickering candle, suffer from cold and hunger. She requested confirmation of the existence of their mother-son relationship, an order for the defendant to pay alimony of one hundred yuan per month, and reimbursement of five thousand yuan for previous educational expenses. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Yuhai opened a court hearing. The plaintiff, Wang Shi, was sixty-three years old, appearing old and frail, with a hunched back, and entered the courtroom, tremblingly stating the facts of the lawsuit. When she reached the most heartbreaking parts, she burst into tears and choked with sobs. The defendant, Wang Changlin, did not appear in person, but was represented by a lawyer who admitted that he had been adopted by the plaintiff as her son in the past, but claimed that this had been canceled later, and there was a written agreement, so the mother-son relationship no longer existed. He requested that the lawsuit be dismissed. Judge Zhang believed that the plaintiff and defendant belonged to different generations and should not be involved in litigation for so long, which would only increase animosity. He instructed them to try to reach a settlement outside of court. The case was adjourned until December 5th for further examination.

Gu Zhuxuan's Appeal Has Been Lodged; The Trial Date Should Not Be Far Off 149

Gu Zhuxuan, the owner of the Tianchan Stage, was accused by Zhao Guangfu, the former manager of the Great World amusement center, in the case of Tang Jiapeng's murder, of instigating the killing. He was arrested by the police and sent to the Second Special Court for public prosecution. After the trial concluded, Gu Zhuxuan was sentenced to fifteen years in prison for instigating murder, with ten years of deprivation of civil rights. Because Gu did not accept the verdict, he submitted a petition to the original court, declaring an appeal. The Second Special Court compiled the case files and submitted them to the higher Third Branch Court for review. He also submitted a supplementary appeal statement, the details of which have been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that Gu Zhuxuan has hired lawyers Shan Yuhua and Wu Qilun to draft an appeal statement, stating ten reasons for disagreeing with the original verdict, totaling several thousand words. The draft has been completed, and the formal lawsuit, using more than ten sheets of paper, has been bound into a thick volume. Yesterday, family members took it to the detention center to request a meeting. After the center issued a permit, they went to Guangci Hospital to have Gu Zhuxuan sign and seal the lawsuit. Then, it was submitted to the Third Branch Court. His defense lawyers also submitted a request to review the case files. Water Dispute in Jingsui Alley; Tenants and Landlords Involved in Lawsuit 150

The houses in the Jingsui Alley area of Songpan Road in Eastern Shanghai are owned by Sun Hechai. Li Hainan, a tenant from Jiangbei, operates a public bathhouse ("tiger stove") in the alley. Because Li was suspected of privately burying water pipes underground to steal water, Sun reported him to the Yangshupu Police Station. The head detective sent officers to arrest him and bring him to the First Special Court for questioning. The judge instructed Li to post bail and adjourned the hearing. Judge Zhan Liangce personally inspected the area the afternoon before last to investigate the matter. It is now known that Li Liangnan has also hired lawyer Jia Yaoxi to file a lawsuit with the First Special Court, accusing landlord Sun Hechai of false accusation and disrupting the water supply, thereby disturbing the peace. The reason given is that Li rents Sun's house to operate a tiger stove, paying a monthly rent of twenty yuan, including the water supply. Because Li sells hot water, he also pays an additional fifteen yuan for water each month. However, starting in February of last year, Li, in order to save on water expenses, directly installed a water meter with the water company and paid according to the meter reading. At the same time, he stopped paying the additional fifteen yuan. The defendant, Sun Hechai, should provide the tenants in Li's building with the water supply they are entitled to. Unexpectedly, recently, all the tenants in Jingsui Alley, due to the poor economy, demanded that Sun reduce the rent and refused to pay it, which angered Sun. On the first of this month, he falsely accused Li Hainan of stealing water at the police station. The police arrested and interrogated Li, who was later released on bail. Furthermore, the next day, Sun, accompanied by workers, suddenly arrived at Li's place and removed the water pipes, including those for the rent, cutting off the water supply. This violates Articles 169 and 304 of the Criminal Law and should be investigated according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan opened a court hearing for this case. The defendant, Sun Hechai, arrived with lawyer Lang Peng to defend him. The court adjourned the case for further hearing.

Opium Smoking Banned in All Hotels in the Public Concession Starting Today; Hotel Staff to Report to Front Desk, Who Will Secretly Report to Police by Phone 152

The Chief Inspector of the Public Concession Police Department, having previously received a letter from Mayor Wu of Shanghai requesting assistance in suppressing opium, has not only dispatched police officers to investigate, but has also summoned managers of major hotels in the concession to the Central Police Station for questioning. Gold Price Soars, Increasing Costs; Woolen Goods, Records, and Other Industries Raise Prices 153

Woolen Industry to Implement Price Hikes Tomorrow; Record Prices to Increase on [Next] Month's [First] Day

Since the gold price has soared, the cost of imported raw materials has risen sharply due to the shrinking foreign exchange rate. Therefore, industries such as bakeries in this city have already implemented price increases to maintain their capital. Now, the cotton and woolen textile industry and record companies such as Great Wall Records have also announced price increases. Details are as follows:

Gloves

The four factories in this city—Zhongnan, Meifeng, Dechang, and Fanlong—jointly issued a statement regarding the price increase of leather gloves, stating: "We hereby inform you that this year's prices were already low. Now, due to the soaring cost of raw materials, which has increased by more than 30%, our industry has decided to increase the old prices by one cost, starting from November 15th, to maintain our capital." (The rest omitted)

Woolen

Zhongnan Cotton and Woolen Textile Factory issued a notice stating: "Since the government order that national currency be based on silver and legal tender be circulated, the soaring cost of various raw materials has been unexpected. As a result, the prices of our factory's products, originally set, can no longer be sustained. To maintain our capital and slightly compensate for losses, we have decided to increase the prices of various woolen sweaters, vests, and scarves by 10% starting from November 15th." (The rest omitted) Huarong Woolen Factory also issued a similar notice.

Records

Great Wall Record Company issued a notice stating: "The Great Wall records issued by our company are manufactured in Germany. Payments to the factory are settled in British pounds. Recently, due to the shrinking foreign exchange rate, the cost has risen sharply. To maintain our capital, we have no choice but to moderately increase the selling price. We have now decided to increase the price by 20 cents (Chinese currency) per record starting from December 1st. Whether it is door-to-door sales, existing orders, or wholesale, the price will be increased uniformly. For remote provinces such as Yunnan, Guizhou, Gansu, Shaanxi, and Sichuan, the implementation will be extended to December 16th."

Municipal Police Bureau Cracks Down on Illegal Employment Agencies; Investigation Underway, Registration to Begin Next Month 154

The Municipal Police Bureau previously considered that the employment agencies (i.e., "reed head shops") in this city were of mixed quality, leading to illegal acts such as kidnapping and selling women, which was extremely regrettable. Therefore, starting last month, it began to rectify them. Each branch bureau reported the number of employment agencies within its jurisdiction to the bureau for preparation for dispatching investigators. The total number of employment agencies reported by each branch bureau is now two hundred. In addition to ordering the few branch bureaus that have not yet reported to do so quickly, the Municipal Police Bureau originally planned to start the review work on the first of this month. However, due to incomplete reporting procedures, it has been slightly delayed. It is now planning to dispatch personnel to conduct investigations with the police of each branch bureau. This will begin in the coming days. Illegal and reckless employment agencies will be severely cracked down on. To protect legally established agencies, registration of employment agencies will be held starting on the first of next month. Those who are approved for registration can continue to operate; those who are not approved will be ordered to cease operations.

Ningbo Industrial Bank's First Batch of Repayments to End; Second Batch of 500 Yuan and Below to Begin Soon 155

After the Shanghai Ningbo Industrial Bank temporarily suspended receipt and payment due to market fluctuations, it was revived by giants from Ningbo, such as Chu Qiqing and Chen Zhonggao, who initiated the organization of a preparatory office. Since the resumption of business, it has received the sympathy of various depositors, and various procedures have been put in order. It has also reported to the Ministry of Finance for approval, which ordered it to first return 20% of the savings deposits in cash according to the proportion of total depositors. It is now known that the revival preparatory office began to verify and issue payments on the 10th of this month. However, due to the large number of depositors, in order to avoid chaotic procedures, the office decided to handle it in batches. The first batch will be paid to depositors with deposits of 100 yuan or less. Therefore, depositors have flocked to the office to receive payments in recent days. There are also many whose addresses are unknown and whose original letters have been returned. Depositors with deposits of more than 100 yuan who have not received a payment notice from the office must bring their deposit certificates and seals to the preparatory office within five days to negotiate the verification and issuance of payment. After the first batch is completed, the second batch of depositors with deposits of 500 yuan or less will be issued immediately. The office will send another letter to notify each depositor to wait. It is said that debtors of the office are using various fine furs, fashionable silk clothes, and steel thermos bottles, etc., to repay their debts. These items are displayed inside the office, and depositors can purchase them without a certificate. Relatives and friends of depositors are also allowed to purchase them. In addition to the discounted prices, there will be an additional 50% discount.

Medical World 170

People's Education Hall Benefits the Poor and Sick—The Shanghai Municipal People's Education Hall pays great attention to the health of citizens. In addition to having Western doctor Sheng Xizhi and Chinese doctor He Lisan specially contracted by the hall to treat patients at any time, it has also recently agreed with the Shanghai South Charity Association's medical treatment and medicine dispensing department to implement a half-price sale method for the sake of the patients. It is heard that the procedure is as follows: on the mornings of every even-numbered day in the Gregorian calendar, patients go to the hall to register. If a Chinese doctor's consultation is required, they can pay the medicine fee, which is 20 cents per dose, and write down their address. Then, the hall's workers will send it to the Shanghai South Charity Association to dispense the medicine. After the association prepares the medicine, it will send it directly to the patient's home for them to take at 3 or 4 PM on the same day. This move is both economical and convenient for patients.

Incoming Correspondence

The Path to Political System Reform (Continued) 172

— Pan Gongzhan

(Shanghai, November of the 24th Year)

—Respectfully Dedicated to the Comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang and the Gentlemen Who Like to Discuss Political System Reform—

Fourth, even if the national crisis is entirely due to the Kuomintang's grasp of political power, "Party Rule" and "Tutelage Politics" should not be held solely responsible as the primary culprits. Because, realistically speaking, in the past few years, we have faced the covetous gaze of powerful neighbors, intensifying foreign troubles, rampant banditry, and pressing internal worries. If this is considered a failure of the Kuomintang, it is more accurately a failure of "one party without governance" than a failure of "Party Rule," and a failure of "politics without tutelage" rather than a failure of "Tutelage Politics." Therefore, in my humble opinion, to save the nation from peril and reverse its unfortunate fate, spending all our energy on debating and pre-announcing a written constitution on paper is less effective than openly and honestly burying ourselves in hard work, starting from strengthening the internal unity of the Party and implementing its political program to achieve the practical effects of "Party Rule," and from preparing for local self-governance and cultivating the people's capabilities to achieve the goals of "Tutelage Politics." If the members of the Kuomintang Central Committee can consistently demonstrate a spirit of unity, as they did at the Sixth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee, and work diligently together, the people will undoubtedly support them. If the Kuomintang's policies for enriching national strength and cultivating popular capabilities can consistently demonstrate decisive power, like the currency reform plan, the people will undoubtedly be happy to follow them. If the Kuomintang's local party branches can truly assist local governments in serving the people, establishing schools everywhere in the shortest possible time, enlightening the people, reviving rural areas, and providing disaster relief, so that the intelligence and wealth of the majority of the people increase, the people will undoubtedly be willing to accept this, and local self-governance will inevitably be achieved. If the people in all localities can govern themselves and support the central government and willingly follow its policies, then the whole nation, united in heart and mind, can naturally achieve the goal of saving the nation from peril. It is clear that to resolve the current national crisis, the Kuomintang in power simply needs to strive diligently, which can be done without blaming heaven or earth for the national crisis, and even less by following the crowd, losing self-confidence, and joining the chorus of self-criticism regarding the unsuitability of "Party Rule" and "Tutelage Politics."

Above, I have pointed out the errors in the theoretical basis of the political system reform theories advocated by those who oppose the Three Principles of the People, layer by layer. Readers may think that I am not advocating for political system reform, but that is not the case. While I do not believe that the political system is omnipotent and that national affairs can be revived simply by reforming the political system, I also believe that the political system is a product of experience, and that for every increment of experience, the political system should be improved to strive for "perfection." Moreover, the philosophy of "when things are exhausted, change occurs, and change leads to progress" can sometimes be applied to the political system. Therefore, to adapt to the current environment, seeking out the shortcomings of the current political system and striving for its improvement is naturally something we should support. However, I believe that reforming the current political system should keep two major principles in mind, which must be explained first: (To be continued)

A Visit to a Glass Factory 173

— Lou Lizhai

—Central Chemical Glass Factory—

During the Qianlong era of the late Qing Dynasty, the central government invested hundreds of thousands of yuan to establish a glass factory in Boshan, Shandong, hiring British technicians to manufacture glass utensils. This was the beginning of China's glass industry. However, the factory's products were limited to snuff bottles for the idle and skylight tiles for buildings, failing to meet the needs of the general public, leading to business failure and closure due to losses. At that time, the dismissed workers, forced by livelihood, used their skills and experience to manufacture some glass utensils at home. However, their intelligence was weak, and they lacked sufficient capital. Regarding manufacturing equipment and technology, they could only adhere to established methods and could not improve them. Therefore, to this day, their descendants can only make paperweights and other materials.

In recent years, the glass industry, like other industries, has made considerable progress. There are glass factories in Tianjin, Beijing, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Fuzhou, Changsha, Suqian, Tangshan, and other places. In terms of quantity, it cannot be considered small. However, there are not many products that can compete with foreign goods, and even fewer that can produce glass for chemical and optical applications. The Central Chemical Glass Factory in Shanghai specializes in chemical glass. Most of the various glass utensils produced by the factory are for chemical and medical use. Although the factory has not been in operation for long and is not large in scale, its products have been certified by the Shanghai Industrial Testing Institute as being of excellent quality and suitable for scientific experiments.

On the afternoon of October 16th, a group of three of us took the museum's car, departed from the museum, passed Tilanqiao, entered Pingliang Road, and drove to the intersection of Ningguo Road, where we got out in front of the factory gate. After being announced, we were greeted by Mr. Xu Xinzhi, the manager, and Mr. Wang Zhengxi, the factory director. They were both wearing very plain clothes, especially Mr. Wang, who was wearing a very dirty blue cloth shirt and trousers. Seeing these very dirty clothes, we could imagine the scene of Mr. Wang directing the workers and burying himself in hard work.

The two gentlemen received us very diligently. After a brief exchange of pleasantries, they led us to visit the various sections.

A glass factory is different from ordinary factories in that all products must be produced from the furnace. The raw materials in the furnace must first be mixed and stirred by the engineer, and then placed in crucibles and sent into the furnace to burn ten hours in advance. Therefore, they first led us to visit the raw material room.

The important raw materials for glass are quartz powder and fluorite powder. In the raw material room, in addition to a lot of these things piled up separately, there were also piles of pre-mixed raw materials, ready to be sent into the furnace to burn.

We walked out of the raw material room and went to the furnace room, where we saw many workers surrounding the blood-red furnace, doing different work. Some people took some molten glass material that had been burned blood-red from the crucible with a hollow iron rod, blew on it, shook it a few times, and then put it in an iron mold and blew on it. After a while, they took it out, and it formed a utensil. Some people were making high-footed wine glasses and various hot water cups, and some people were pulling glass tubes, pulling them very long, and then cutting them to the required length. Behind the furnace room, there were three large drying rooms, which were specially used for tempering the finished utensils. Because the temperature of the utensils made from the raw materials taken from the furnace is very high, it must be allowed to cool down slowly. Therefore, some workers were sending the newly made utensils into the drying room. All finished utensils can be taken out after spending twenty-four hours in the drying room for further work.

After we finished watching the situation in the furnace room, Mr. Xu and Mr. Wang led us to the engraving room, where we saw many machines lined up, and many workers surrounding the machines doing various different jobs. Some were engraving very fine patterns on glass cups, and some were polishing the mouths of glass cups.

Next, we went to the measuring instrument engraving room, where we saw two or three workers engraving ten cc measuring cylinders and one cc droppers with one hundred graduations on the machines. This kind of work is very precise. Next to the measuring instrument engraving room was the gas workshop, where many workers were making condenser tubes and the mouths of measuring flasks. According to Mr. Xu and Mr. Wang, this kind of craft is very difficult to do, so the workers in this section are paid very well, with the highest salary reaching 180 yuan per month, which is much higher than the salaries of the manager and the factory director.

Finally, the two gentlemen also led us to the packaging room to see the packaging situation.

After we finished watching the production process, Mr. Xu told us that the factory was initiated by several people who loved science. Preparations began in September of the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), and it was established in July of the 23rd year (1934), with a capital of 50,000 yuan. The target of the business is the academic and medical community, and household utensils are not particularly emphasized. From the opening to the end of last year, the turnover reached more than 100,000 yuan in half a year. Since this year, the business has made great progress, and 70% of the universities in the country have adopted the factory's products.

After listening to these words, we deeply feel that in today's era when the Chinese people are vigorously promoting science, it is a blessing for China that the Chinese people can manufacture their own scientific instruments to promote China's science. We hope that the scientific community can adopt them more to develop China's science. Note: (There are a few words to add from the "Overview of Shanghai's Textile Industry" edited by the China Credit Information Institute) According to Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company, since the shutdown last winter, it has repeatedly sought to resume operations. At the beginning of last month, Du Yuesheng and others rose up to organize the Textile Industry Banking Group to actively assist. It has already started work on the 23rd of the same month.

Education News

National Social Education in the 21st Year 174

The Ministry of Education's statistics on various social education undertakings across the country in the 21st year are divided into school-style social education institutions (including people's schools, literacy centers, agricultural, commercial, and industrial supplementary schools, women's supplementary schools, training centers or classes for physical education and phonetic symbols, training centers or classes for opera and storytelling, orphan and poor children's homes, drama schools, training centers or classes for social education and mass education personnel, schools for the mentally disabled, deaf-mute, and reformatory, and other supplementary schools belonging to the scope of social education), and general social education institutions (including people's literacy and writing centers, people's reading rooms, popular lecture halls, people's tea gardens, parks, libraries, educational museums, art galleries, public sports, public entertainment, cinemas, etc., music and sports clubs, mass education experimental zones, swimming pools, theaters, antique preservation institutes, and other social education institutions). There are a total of 84,212 public and private institutions (public institutions include provincial, county, and municipal institutions), with a total public and private expenditure of 20,979,026 yuan. There are a total of 136,206 public and private institution teachers and staff, and 1,298,467 public and private school students (this item only includes students belonging to school-style social education institutions). From this statistic, and with reference to previous years' investigations, the following conclusions can be drawn: (1) The number of social education institutions across the country has increased from more than 10,000 to more than 84,000 in the past five years, approximately eight times the original number. (2) The amount of social education funding across the country has increased from more than 3.6 million yuan to more than 20 million yuan in the past five years, approximately five times the original amount. (3) The number of teachers and staff in social education institutions across the country has increased from more than 14,000 to more than 134,000 in the past five years, approximately nine times the original number. (4) The number of students in social education institutions across the country has increased from more than 219,000 to more than 1,298,000 in the past five years, approximately five times the original number. (5) Among the social education institutions that increased the most this year compared to last year, people's schools accounted for the most, with an increase of more than 2,800 schools. This was followed by people's literacy and writing centers, and people's reading rooms, both of which increased by more than 1,000 centers. (6) Among the social education expenses that increased the most this year compared to last year, orphan and poor children's homes accounted for the most, with an increase of more than 6.58 million yuan. This was followed by people's schools, with an increase of more than 880,000 yuan, and then by educational museums, with an increase of more than 400,000 yuan. (7) Among the teachers and staff in social education institutions that increased the most this year compared to last year, people's schools accounted for the most, with an increase of more than 7,600 people. This was followed by people's literacy and writing centers, with an increase of more than 700 people, and then by literacy centers, with an increase of more than 600 people. (8) Among the students in school-style social education institutions that increased the most this year compared to last year, people's schools accounted for the most, with an increase of more than 47,000 people. This was followed by physical education training centers or classes, with an increase of more than 7,000 people. (9) The provinces with the most social education institutions increased this year were Shandong and Zhejiang, both with an increase of more than 2,000 centers. The province with the most institutions decreased was Sichuan, with a decrease of more than 2,000 centers. (10) The province with the most social education expenses increased this year was Guangdong, with an increase of more than 6.8 million yuan. This was followed by Guangxi, with an increase of more than 480,000 yuan. The province with the most expenses decreased was Sichuan, with a decrease of more than 300,000 yuan. (11) The province with the most staff increased was Hebei, with an increase of more than 5,000 people. The province with the most staff decreased was Sichuan, with a decrease of more than 4,000 people. (12) The provinces with the most students in social education institutions increased this year were Hebei, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu, all with an increase of more than 20,000 people. The province with the most students decreased was Sichuan, with a decrease of more than 20,000 people. (13) Within this year, the cost per graduate in each people's school was the highest in Qinghai, at 39 yuan and 10 cents, and the lowest in Weihaiwei, at 7 yuan and 3 cents. (14) The provinces with social education budget reaching the standard stipulated by the National Government in the 18th year were Hankou, Xikang, Hunan, Tianjin, Fujian, and Nanjing, with a total of six places. In the 19th year, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, and Shaanxi were added, with a total of nine places. In the 20th year, there were six places: Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Weihaiwei, Beijing, Fujian, and Shanghai. In the 21st year, there were five places: Weihaiwei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Qingdao, and Fujian. In the 22nd year, there were six places: Jiangsu, Qingdao, Weihaiwei, Zhejiang, Beijing, and Fujian. In the 23rd year, there were eight places: Weihaiwei, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Beijing, Zhejiang, Guangxi, Fujian, and Henan. (15) This year, the city with the highest average social education expenditure per person per year was Beiping, at 7 jiao, 8 fen, and 5 li, and the lowest was Xikang, at 1 li. The national average expenditure was 7 fen and 8 li.

Regulations for the Preparatory Office for Shanghai Municipal Museum. The decision was made to hand the draft to the Preparatory Office for submission to the Board of Directors for resolution.

The Simple Regulations for the Preparatory Office of the Shanghai Municipal Museum Article 1: The Temporary Board of Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Museum establishes the Preparatory Office for the purpose of facilitating preparations. Article 2: The Preparatory Office shall have one Director and one Deputy Director, who shall be recommended by the Board of Directors and appointed by the Municipal Government. They shall preside over the affairs of the office under the direction of the Chairman of the Board. Article 3: The Preparatory Office shall have three full-time secretaries, three concurrent clerks, and a number of employees to handle preparatory matters. Article 4: The Preparatory Office shall hold a work meeting once every half month, convened by the Director. Temporary meetings may be convened when necessary. Article 5: The preparatory period for the Preparatory Office shall be limited to three months. Article 6: If there are any matters not covered in these Regulations, the Board of Directors may amend them at any time. Article 7: These Regulations shall be submitted to the Government for approval after being resolved by the Board of Directors.

The school suspended classes for the day, and all faculty and students attended to listen to the speeches. First, President Yan gave a speech, and then the competition began. All the students used their eloquent tongues to speak fluently and eloquently. The content of their speeches was wonderful. As a result, Liang Zhitang won first place with his speech on "The Attitude that Vocational Youth Should Have", and received a silver tripod. Jin Shiqing won second place with his speech on "The Deepening National Crisis and the Spirit We Should Have", and received a silver shield. Cheng Hanming won third place with his speech on "The Current State of the Country and the Responsibilities of Our Youth", and received a silver medal. The other participating students each received a bundle of special stationery.

Hubbei Middle School: The number of students in Shanghai Hubbei Primary and Middle School on Qiujiang Road in this city has increased to more than 900 this year. All the faculty and students of the school, feeling the severity of the domestic flood disaster, specially launched a voluntary donation campaign. As a result, a total of more than 150 yuan was collected and has been sent to the Charity Relief Association. It is also learned that the school has added academic lectures this semester. Yesterday, Zhang Yongchun from the Municipal Education Bureau was invited to the school to give a lecture entitled "How to Participate in Speech Contests."

Elementary Education Research Conference in Yinxiang District 189

The Yinxiang District Elementary Education Research Association of this city held its first research conference yesterday. More than 80 principals, teachers, and staff members from seven municipal schools including Hongbei, Qiuxi, Hongzhen, Yinnan, and Jiangqiao, and eight private schools including Shihua, Ningbo Eighth Elementary, Chengyu, Meizhou, Jinghua, Yinbei, Hudong Labor No. 13 attended. Chen Boxiu chaired the meeting, and Tong Shiquan, a special representative from the Municipal Education Bureau, provided guidance. The atmosphere at the meeting was extremely enthusiastic, and the order was well maintained. Many research questions were approved on the spot, and the questions were distributed to each school for detailed study. A written report is to be submitted to the chair school by December 1st. The research questions that each school should study are extracted as follows: (1) What kind of attitude should be adopted during rural family visits? Shihua, Hongbei, Jiangqiao. (2) Prescribe the minimum standards for equipment for each subject. Ningbo Eighth Elementary, Yinxi. (3) How to remedy the impact of excessive absenteeism of students in rural schools on academic progress? Yucai, Meizhou. (4) Is it appropriate to allow lower grade children in the intermittent two-part system to do their homework automatically in the same classroom when teaching directly in other departments? Meizhou, Hongzhen. (5) How to increase literacy opportunities for lower grade children? Yucai, Jinghua. (6) Which is more important, oral or written composition in elementary school, and how should the proportion be distributed? Qiuxi, Yinbei. (7) What materials should be used for advanced crafts in rural elementary schools? Hudong, Yinnan. (8) How to make rural children neat and clean? Hongjiang, Labor.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Man (95) 191

— Louisa M. Alcott, Original Work, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Later the doctor came, and the poor hero went through a hard struggle, because some small bones in his foot were injured, and fixing them was still a painful thing. So Don's lips turned white, and beads of sweat rested on his forehead, but he never cried out, just clutched Mrs. Joe's hand, so it was still red after a long time.

"You have to keep this child very quiet, at least for a week, don't let him put his foot on the ground. By then I can know if he can try hopping along with a cane, or if he needs to rest longer," said the doctor, as he put away the shiny knives and clamps, which Don didn't like to see either.

Don was startled to hear the word crutches, and quickly asked, "Will he get better someday, won't he?"

"Hopefully," said the doctor, and left. Don felt very depressed, because losing a foot was a terrible disaster from the perspective of a lively child.

"Don't worry, I'm a famous nurse, we'll have you walking as usual in a month," said Mrs. Joe, who took an optimistic view of the matter.

But the fear of lifelong disability haunted Don's dreams, and even Tenty's comfort was not enough to lift his spirits; so Mrs. Joe suggested that a few children come in to visit, and asked him which ones he would like to see.

"Ned and Joe; I also love my hat, and there are some things inside that I think they'd like to see too. I guess you threw away my bag of loot?" said Don, his face suddenly anxious when he asked the question.

Iron City Cup Basketball Tournament - 14 Teams Have Registered 192

The organizing committee held its first meeting yesterday and will start accepting applications immediately, with a deadline of the 25th.

The Iron City Cup Basketball Tournament, organized by the Shanghai Sports Association, convened representatives of various well-known basketball teams in the city at the Youth Association on Baxianqiao on the ninth floor yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, and organized a preparatory committee to hold its first preparatory meeting, deciding on the main points of the competition regulations. Registration will begin immediately and will close on the 25th of this month. Details are listed as follows:

Team Representatives' Meeting

The meeting of team representatives was held at 3:00 PM. Those present included Jiang Jianbai, Tai Rugan, Jiang Wan Chen Dede, Xu Heng from the Municipal Sports Association, Jiang Liangui from Dongya, Wang Fudan from Chizhi, Chen Hongchang from the Law School, Hu Zongfan from Huadong, Zhou Junren from Chizhi High School, Shen Guoquan (Peng Wenyu as a representative) from Jiaotong University, Peng Yushan from Guanghua, Zhang Yuansheng from Liangjiang, Shi Zhiqian from Tongji, and Shi Yunlong from Southeast. Chairman Jiang Jianbai first gave a report with Tai Rugan, and then decided (1) to establish the Iron City Cup Basketball Tournament Preparatory Committee, with the Municipal Sports Association hiring Yu Hengzhi, Chen Bingde, Shen Guoquan, Ding Liangxian, and Wang Fudan as members, (2) the competition will be temporarily divided into men's and women's A and B groups, (3) no registration fee will be charged, only a deposit of five yuan per team will be collected, and will be returned at the end of the tournament, (4) the referees will be decided by the refereeing department of the preparatory committee based on the actual situation, (5) the start date of the competition will be decided by the preparatory committee, and will end before the winter vacation of this year, (6) the preparatory committee's office will be located at the Municipal Sports Association.

First Preparatory Meeting

The first preparatory meeting was held afterwards, attended by Tai Rugan, Yu Hengzhi (Shen Kunnan as a representative), Wang Fudan, Jiang Liangui, Chen Bingde, Shen Guoquan (Peng Wenyu as a representative), Chairman Tai Rugan, (1) job assignments: Chen Bingde and Jiang Liangui will be in charge of the refereeing department, Wang Fudan and Shen Guoquan will be in charge of the scheduling department, and Wang Keyong and Hu Zongfan will be invited to be in charge of the venue equipment department. Other staff will be concurrently served by the staff of the Municipal Sports Association, (2) The main points of the Iron City Cup Basketball Tournament regulations are determined as follows:

Main Points of Competition Regulations

(1) Grouping: Both men and women are divided into Group A and Group B. When there are more teams participating in the men's division, they will be held in multiple divisions, (2) Number of registrants: Each men's team can have up to 12 players, and each women's team can have up to 15 players, (3) Deposit: No registration fee will be charged, a deposit of five yuan will be paid upon registration, and will be returned at the end of the competition, but teams that forfeit more than twice will have their deposit confiscated, (4) Registration date: Registration will begin immediately and close on the 15th of this month. Mail-in registrations must be properly addressed, (5) Registration location: Shanghai Sports Association Office (inside the Municipal Central District Education Bureau), (6) Competition method: a single round-robin system will be adopted, (7) Competition rules: the latest rules promulgated by the Chinese National Sports Association will be adopted, (8) Competition venue: the gymnasium of the Municipal Central District Sports Ground, (9) Competition balls: domestic goods will be used, (10) Uniforms: each team provides their own, the colors must be uniform, and must be specified at the time of registration. The numbers on the uniforms must be in accordance with the basketball rules, (11) Players of each team may not be changed after the start of the competition, (12) The competition will end by the end of October, and may be extended if necessary, (13) The competition time is from 4:00 PM to 9:00 PM. Each team should indicate the most suitable time and the next most suitable time on the registration form, (14) The competition time cannot be changed after it is announced. In case of special circumstances, the change must be approved by the preparatory committee with a legitimate reason, (15) In addition to the Iron City Cup, all championship team members will each be awarded a medal from the association.

Fourteen Teams Have Registered

Overview of Guangdong Provincial Sports College 200

Huang Linshu, Director of the Department of Education of Guangdong Province, in order to cultivate specialized sports talents and develop the sports industry in the province, specially established two sports colleges, and hired Chen Lianglie, Cheng Yue'en, Deng Mingjie, Zhang Zhongren, Xu Minhua, Huang Qiming and other famous figures in the education circles of the province as preparatory committee members. The school has now been established after preparation. The following is a brief description of the school:

(1) School Buildings and Equipment: The school is located at the old site of the Guangdong Provincial Games on the East School Field in Guangzhou, covering hundreds of acres. There is one track and field field, one football field, three basketball fields, and four volleyball fields, with several grandstands built around the periphery. Other sports equipment is available. The construction cost is estimated at more than 200,000 yuan, making it the best sports field in the province. Since the Guangdong Provincial Education Authority decided to establish a sports college, it allocated the old site of the association to the school, and allocated an additional 180,000 yuan for the construction of classrooms, dormitories and other places. The buildings that have now been completed include four classrooms and one dormitory, washroom, and bathroom each. Those that are planned and under construction include one auditorium, gym, school office, dining hall, faculty dormitory, and library each, four classrooms, three dormitories for male and female students, and sports equipment storage rooms, kitchens, guardhouses, bathrooms, toilets, and other facilities.

(2) School Organization: The school has one president, under whom there are two departments: academic affairs and administrative affairs, each with a director of academic affairs and a director of administrative affairs, and a number of full-time professors, lecturers, and teaching assistants. Students are divided into three classes: specialized subjects, teacher training, and training courses, each with 50 students. Each class has one head teacher, who is also a full-time professor. In addition, under the Academic Affairs and Administrative Affairs Departments, there are registration, statistics, military training, documents, accounting, general affairs, medical, and library sections, each with one director and several staff members, who are responsible for the work of each department.

(3) Current Faculty and Staff: The school's faculty and staff are all sports celebrities hired from Shanghai. The current president, Xu Minhua, has a Master of Physical Education from Springfield College in the United States, and has served as the director of physical education at National Tsinghua, Northeast, and Soochow Universities. He is currently also the sports supervisor of the province. Liu Xuesong, director of academic affairs, also has a Master of Physical Education from Springfield College, and has served as the director of physical education and professor at various universities in China. Qu Yue, director of administrative affairs, has served as a standing director of the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council and director of the East Asia Sports College. Yu Jie, a full-time professor, is also a sports celebrity in Shanghai. Other faculty and staff are also well-known figures in the sports circles of China.

(4) Student Overview: The school currently has 40 specialized students, 50 teacher training students, and 50 training course students. Specialized students graduate in two years, with graduates of senior middle schools being qualified. Teacher training students graduate in three years, with graduates of junior middle schools being qualified. Training course students graduate in one year, with those who have served as middle school physical education teachers for three years or elementary school physical education teachers for five years with outstanding results being qualified. Although the school enrolled 150 students this fall, the number of applicants reached more than 700, and because the selection was too strict, only 140 were qualified.

Finance: The Chips Loosen, the Expiration Nears; the Standard Gold Price Plunges Sharply 205

Hedgers Heavily Short; Major Buyers' Interest Wanes; Floating Long Positions Waver; Final Drop of Six Yuan and Three Jiao

The gold market has been peaceful for several days, but yesterday there was a slight decline, mainly because large holders had already cut their long positions, and Chinese merchants were arbitraging U.S. dollars, loosening the chips. The expiration date is pressing, and the long side is easily shaken. According to morning reports from overseas silver markets, both British and American markets were flat. The forward silver prices in Monterrey varied. Exchange rates were slightly long. London refined gold rose two pence. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with both British and American rates flat. The Customs Gold Unit rose four li. The standard gold price was posted at a premium of 1149 yuan and 3 jiao. However, market sentiment did not improve. The market opened slightly lower in the morning. After the opening, major holders and banks offered gold together, and the price declined. However, buyers were still active, and the price rebounded slightly. It was anticipated that the HSBC exchange rate would be announced, with the British rate flat and the American rate up by .0625. Afterward, banks continued to sell and major holders continued to sell bullion, eventually leading to a decline. However, the market was peaceful, and fluctuations were limited. The Bank of Japan squared its sterling position, and the situation stabilized slightly after the initial decline. The silver equalization tax remained unchanged. Although the Hong Kong market did not appear favorable, the demand was scarce, leaving no room for activity. It was predicted that Indian silver would remain unchanged. Banks traded amongst themselves, making the market even more idle and seemingly stable. The market was quieter at noon. In the afternoon, due to tight exchange rates, the market showed signs of firmness. Major holders took advantage of the high price to sell bullion, and banks seized the opportunity to sell, preventing further gains. Although the Hong Kong market was firm, Indian silver was reported flat. The overall situation stabilized, with little fluctuation. Indian silver remained flat in the second report. Major holders supplied gold, causing a slight decline, but the price still hovered. The supply side became more active, but there was a lack of buyers. At two o'clock, sellers gathered, and rumors spread, causing a sudden drop to 1142 yuan. Exchange rates were peaceful, and there were many who bought to cover at the lower price, making it easy to push the price up. The market ultimately remained indecisive, mainly because unfounded rumors spooked the gold market, and the long side was pressured by the impending expiration date, making it easily shaken. Today will begin the December expiration rollover date. It is predicted beforehand that the short side will offer around ten yuan. The day's market situation is recorded as follows:

The morning opening was 1148 yuan, down 9 jiao from the previous close. Hengchang Yong accepted bullion at 8 yuan and 5 jiao. Wanfeng Jinlong Yingfu Tongfeng Heng sold bullion. It was anticipated that the HSBC Bank's official exchange rate would be announced, with the British rate flat and the American rate up by .0625. Although the Hong Kong market was loose, Hongxing Yong entered, rising from 6 yuan and 9 jiao to 7 yuan and 3 jiao. Tongfeng Heng and others still had supplies. It was predicted that Indian silver would remain unchanged, leading to stagnation. After hovering, the noon close was 1147 yuan and 1 jiao.

According to foreign reports, London large bars were flat for both near and far terms. The New York silver market remained unchanged. The Hong Kong market became firmer. The Indian silver telegraph reported that it would remain unchanged. Banks took advantage of the high price to sell, and there was much fluctuation.
