Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Tokyo Correspondence 222

Impressions After Watching "Koxinga's Battles" 223

— Fang Xun

In early September, the commercial theaters in Tokyo have already begun their autumn "battles." Among the many staged programs, the ones that are more attractive are the "Bride School," written by Kataoka Teppei, directed by Senda Koreya, and starring Mizutani Yaeko, which is being performed at the Meiji-za Theater; "Nata," written by Mafune Yutaka, directed by Kubota Mantaro, which is being performed at the Tokyo Theater; "Shunkinsho," written by Tanizaki Junichiro, directed by Tagomura Rokuro; "A Kesas no Ryo-nin," written by Kikuchi Kan, directed by Mizuki Kumio, which is being performed at the Yurakuza Theater; and "Koxinga's Battles," written by Osanai Kaoru, directed by Sonoike Kagyo and Aoyagi Nobuo. Because the other programs at the Meiji-za Theater were uninteresting, and I originally wanted to see "Shunkinsho" at the Tokyo Theater, but firstly, I could not get used to the male impersonating female tone of "New School Drama (Japanese civilization play)," and secondly, I was unwilling to sit for five or six hours in the air of "Takashimade" and "Momowari" (Note: names of old-style Japanese hairstyles). (Most of the audience of the New School Drama are people from the entertainment industry; just like in China, when famous actors appear on stage, there are strange shouts of applause from the audience, and the plays performed are limited to so-called human tragedy.) At the same time, I thought that Tanizaki's original work was staged on this occasion, it was already "the song of the Shu-uguisu bird" "not at the right time, not in the right place" (words of the protagonist Shunkin in the original work), so I only went to see "Koxinga's Battles," which was co-performed by the former Kabuki famous actor Sumizō and Natsukawa Shizue.

I think it is very interesting that this play is being staged at this time.

The story is taken from the late Ming Dynasty in China. "Si Zong's favored minister Li Taotian colluded with the Tartars, invaded China, and killed Si Zong in the forbidden palace. Grand Sima General Wu Sangui killed his own son to replace the young emperor, so he was spared from the disaster. The emperor's sister Zhantan, with the help of Wu Sangui's wife Liu Gejun, took a boat across the sea and arrived in Hirado, Japan, first. Zhi Long, a Ming minister, was trapped by traitors, and he went to Japan quickly, and he had already married and had children. The son's name is Wazanei (i.e., Zheng Chenggong). He is resourceful, brave and invincible. Seeing Zhantan coming, he knew that the Ming Dynasty had collapsed, so Zhi Long led his wife and children back to China, and sought to see Gan Qinghui's eldest daughter Jin Xiang, who was married to Zheng Chenggong. Tell Gan Hui to help Cheng Gong restore Ming Yin, Gan Hui also has the ambition to restore the country, but is unwilling to unite with the 'Japanese' Wazanei because of his wife and children. Jin Xiang then cut her abdomen to show her determination, and Wazanei's mother killed herself with a knife to prevent her son from having any worries. Wazanei then led the three armies to drive away the Tartars, restore the Ming Dynasty, and was named Koxinga, the Prince of Yanping, for his功."

This story is not Osanai's creation. Before him, similar structures had already appeared in "Joruri" and Chikamatsu Monzaemon's "Kabuki". Osanai's adaptation is roughly based on Chikamatsu's Kabuki. As far as the story is concerned, we already feel a bit absurd and unfounded, but we did not expect that Mr. Osanai, the founder of the Japanese New Drama Movement, would arrange the "Improved Kabuki" in such a mixed and chaotic manner. Mr. Osanai's performance technique originally originated from Stanislavsky's school, but he, who is usually so careful and meticulous, took such a big risk here! In addition to the original Kabuki and Gidayu of Japan, this play also uses Chinese musical accompaniment, Chinese opera fighting, and Acrobat. It is said that it also adopted the expression methods of fingers and movements from Mei Lanfang's Chinese opera. In the stage setting, it also explained Osanai's school of old realism and adopted an extremely simplified method. During the fighting, the stuntman uses the same somersault, tiger jump, but after a while, there is a Nanyang-style music. In the drama, I don't feel any inscription, and the spectacle is not necessarily brilliant, so why do you want to perform this kind of drama?

Let us now put aside whether the historical facts are true or not. First, according to the current performance, we feel that in addition to uglifying and 　forcing the power of the Chinese nation, there is no other significance. The most sympathetic and sanctified character in the play is Wazanei's mother (Japanese), and the most heroic character is Wazanei himself, who wears Japanese clothes. For example, in the scene of fighting a tiger in the bamboo forest (it is clear that this is from 　Yang　), it is not Wazanei's "human power" that conquers the big tiger, but the divine power of the Ise Great God's "amulet" (a kind of Mascot) given to him by his mother! For example, when Zheng Zhilong changed into Ming Dynasty clothes in a city building, the purpose was entirely to promote the Japanese woman's virtues and spirit of Wazanei's mother from the contrast in front of the full house of "Tang people"!

In addition to these commercial theaters, the performances of experimental theater troupes, such as the September performance of "Creation Theater" and the one-year anniversary performance of "New Association Theater", are mostly in the late month. I hope that the insomnia that erodes my body can be reduced a little, and perhaps I can report more energetic Tokyo theater news to the readers of this journal.

Famous actress Natsukawa Shizue in "Koxinga's Battles" plays Zheng Chenggong's half-sister Zheng Jinxiang. 224

Japan's biggest masterpiece film of the year "Two Wives" (from left to right, Eihakudaiji, Maruyama Sadao) 225

On the Road of New Poetry 226

— Ren Jun

Recently, I read an article by Mr. Chen Zizhan on the issue of new poetry, which is one of "Qu Lu's Poetry Talks" in "Yan Lin" of Li Bao. The main idea of ​​this article is: the current Chinese new poetry world is quite sluggish. "Many advanced new poets have put down their pens, undoubtedly admitting their failure. New poets have not found any new ways, and it is unwise to follow the old ways; therefore, Mr. Chen advises new poets to simply go back to the 'Hu Shi style' that has evolved from old poetry, and in the middle, he especially cited the 'Flying Small Praise', which seems like a small poem written by Hu Shi when he traveled to Guangxi, as the latest specimen of the so-called 'Hu Shi style'."

Indeed, Mr. Chen Zeng declared: "Naturally, it is not said that this is the only way"; but at least this is "a way", and it is "a way that new poets can take" that Mr. Chen does not hesitate to point out specially. There is no doubt about this.

At present, I feel that this kind of opinion is not very appropriate and worthy of discussion.

First of all, it must be pointed out that what Mr. Chen said is somewhat self-contradictory. He deeply believes that it is unwise for new poets not to find new ways and to follow the old ways; but at the same time, he advises new poets to take the "Hu Shi style" way. Is it possible that the "Hu Shi style" is not an "old way"? Is it possible that taking this "old way" counts as "　"?...

Secondly, in terms of the history of the Chinese new poetry movement, everyone knows that as the first experimenter in writing new poetry, Hu Shi's works, due to the relationship between his era and his talent, can be said to be extremely immature, especially with the product of inseparable blood relationship with old poetry. If we compare them with the works of later writers, we cannot deny in terms of content or form that the later new poetry has undoubtedly gradually progressed to a higher stage. Unexpectedly, at this moment, Mr. Chen turned around and called on the new poets to go back and take Hu Shi's old road. I think this not only wipes out the achievements of the new poetry movement that has been painstakingly managed for more than ten years; moreover, to put it more seriously, it also inevitably has the suspicion of deliberately advising people to drive backwards!

I remember that Hu Shi, who was rich in years, once compared those "new critics" who had not been poisoned by old poetry to "little girls with natural feet" in the preface to the fourth edition of "Attempt Collection", saying that their creations "are bold in liberation and full of fresh meaning, which makes me happy and ashamed"; and he compared himself to a "woman who had her feet bound and then released", frankly admitting that his poems "still carry the bloody air of the foot-binding era". If his metaphor is still appropriate, then Mr. Chen Zizhan is no different from calling us "little girls with natural feet" to re-learn how to walk like a "woman who had her feet bound and then released", and to seep out some "bloody air of the foot-binding era" on our feet again!

It is true that the current Chinese new poetry world is quite sluggish. Although there are quite a few reasons for this, those who write poetry cannot but bear considerable responsibility. ——Literature and art (poetry is naturally no exception) is a reflection of reality. The more a work can correctly and profoundly reflect objective reality, the more meaningful and valuable it will be. However, in fact, there are quite a few in China today. Poets simply dare not or "disdain" to look reality in the eye with their "noble" eyes. They still sit high in the supreme ivory tower all day long: or they specialize in chanting about the wind and the moon, trying to put the moldy old wine into new bottles, or they hum some flowers, crows, girls, and seven-stringed guqin as usual, and they also claim to be what school and what school, deliberately making their texts mysterious, deliberately showing off their so-called "novel techniques", and writing many "beautiful" poems that "low-energy" readers do not understand. This is a phenomenon. In addition, there are also some poets who, although they have a correct worldview and ideology to a certain extent; but their lives are still lacking, their experiences are still insufficient, and their works are prone to being empty; or they have not grasped the most appropriate expression methods, and cannot "cash in" the specific theme into concrete images, so it is difficult to write satisfactory works. This is another phenomenon. —Our poets' activities are already in such a situation, so what's so strange about the sluggishness of the current new poetry world!

Therefore, I feel that for today's Chinese new poets, the most important thing is to bravely face reality, and to enrich their lives as much as possible on the one hand, and to conquer brand-new techniques in creative activities on the other. Only in this way can we achieve greater achievements and open up a more open future for new poetry!

As for the "Hu Shi style", I think it is already a historical "antique", and it is definitely not a way, definitely not a way that our new poets should take at present.

Life and Love 227

— Yan Yilin

The writer Mary Coleridge, in an article entitled "The King Is Dead, Long Live The King", narrates a meaningful story: Once upon a time, there was a king who died when he was very young. He felt that it was not the time for him to die, not because he had a beautiful wife, but because he was such an excellent king during his lifetime. He worked day and night, selflessly planning for the welfare of all the people in his country; in addition, he had many good friends. He thought to himself that his wife, friends, and all the people in the country needed his resurrection. So he finally got the approval of heaven, allowing him to return to the world. If he could find three people who needed his resurrection within an hour, he would be able to live several more years in the world. He returned to the world, but was completely disappointed. Even his best friend during his lifetime threw his photo on the floor and burned his letters in the stove. His good friend had already gone to serve the new king. His beautiful wife was having a secret meeting with her lover. Everything was completely "beyond expectations". He then realized his stupidity and was willing to sleep sadly on the ground.

Mary Coleridge satirizes the erroneous mentality of people who think their existence is very important in this article. But I think this kind of psychological error is extremely beneficial. Because there is such an error lying in people's hearts, life has a profound meaning. Moreover, the progress of mankind is based on this point; otherwise, everyone will give up the idea of "self-importance", then the entire human race will sink into the twilight of death and become a self-defeating world; perhaps many people will therefore bid farewell to their lives and the world.

It is the most pleasant thing in the world when a person feels that he is needed by others or the world; and he will immediately feel a profound meaning in life. The so-called "love" is to feel that one is needed; ——especially the so-called "love". For those who have experience in this area, they should always remember that when they think of the fact that they are loved by a woman, an unspeakable pleasure suddenly floats in their chest, and they are proud of it. On the contrary, the greatest sadness and sorrow in the world is to discover that you have been abandoned: therefore, suicide after "losing love" is also a common occurrence.

However, are people really not needed by other people? You can get it if you think about it. I don't think it's all like the writer Mary Coleridge showed. If there is such a thing as "love" in the world, it can prove that his is not entirely right.

However, for those who have become the past, it is the law of nature to be forgotten.

White Goose Pool 228

— Li Sanlang

White Goose Pool, White Goose Pool, White Goose Pool.

The warships of the oppressors are always berthed there;

The fire and smoke of foreign media always rises there.

Tall noses, golden hair.

The group of driven slaves.

Guarding our seaport,

Threatening our small warships.

The surging torrent is rolling,

The bell of a certain church on the west bank is ringing,

Hypocritical Christians come again

To comfort the souls of our unfortunate, Amen!

In the foreign paradise-like Shamian,

The singing from the high foreign houses is floating.

But they say:

"This is the home of peaceful people!"

But they forgot that the bloodstains of "June 23rd" have not yet dried.

Now, the shadow of terrible killing is flickering again,

It will not only be the tragic death of passionate young people,

It will unfold in our cities and villages.

White Goose Pool will become a mass grave of floating corpses again.

White Goose Pool, White Goose Pool, White Goose Pool,

You are the fat belly of our unfortunate,

You are the throat that prevents us from breathing.

But, this is full of flags of various colors,

Proudly fluttering on your face.

Ambition 229

— Long Gong

Once, I met two graduating normal school students, a man and a woman, who were a couple. In a suitable setting, we talked about happiness, future aspirations... things young men like to talk about. He spoke of his ideals in a full, sonorous voice.

"Our director of student affairs is also a strange character. He himself smokes opium, runs a sporting goods and stationery shop, and a small restaurant, and is busy all day long, yet he tells the students: 'My ideal is a lifelong revolution.'" Lifelong, how bizarre! ... He likes to bow to the students, and when he lectures them, he says, "Mr. Wang, please do this and that," or "Mr. Li, please do that and that." This fellow is lying.

"Principal Kong Xianren disagrees with the director of student affairs. He says: 'The citizens of a country are like ants in a nest. Magnified under a microscope, they all look different. I hope to be an honest and obedient citizen!' ... Mr. Yang Ruopeng's encouragement is correct, and so am I. — Have you dissected ants?'

"What will be the result of doing other things for life, or being a citizen for life? — They are all wrong, I say. If so, let's think about Guangdong ten years from now... at least five million illiterate, uncivilized children! A country without elementary school teachers! Everyone will become like — alas..."

"Let me talk about myself. I want to be a governor. The first thing I want to do is to raise the salaries of elementary school teachers, stipulate high rates of pay increases, give them the honor of lifetime employment, and insure their lives, illnesses, fires, floods, and war disasters, and announce preferential regulations for them in theaters, teahouses, and various public transportation services... My goal as governor is simple. In addition, I think I can confiscate all firearms from the people, and use this method to avoid dangerous incidents... I want to be like so-and-so in the past, able to walk on the road with only two followers. When people see me, they don't have to point behind my back and whisper, 'This is the governor,' they can walk up to me and say, 'Hello, Governor,' and they can bow or not as they please... In short, I still live my free life as a commoner..."

"But after I got together with her, I gradually changed. Now, I more firmly think that I really want to be an elementary school principal. An elementary school principal. — Easy to understand. She is my assistant, my 'cheering partner.' We... what did you say?"

The girl shrank her head, pouted her lips, squinted her eyes, and made a humming sound in this coy gesture, then she corrected him:

"You might as well honestly tell him that this is my ideal!"

"Okay. — It's the same thing. We only need sixty students. And we won't hire any other teachers... These sixty children are our children, our students, and also our masters. We all live in the school together... For the beauty of their bodies and the beauty of their spirits, there must be spacious school buildings, including a sports field, classrooms, a library, dormitories, a dining hall, a swimming pool, a courtyard, a hall... a small mountain, a small lake, a small river... everywhere is flowers, grass, and trees. Parents entrust their children to the two of us, this is complete trust. We want them to wear the same beautiful clothes, different only in their blue, brown, or black eyes. We want them to breathe civilization from an early age... You know how much those children will love this!"

Regarding the concerns of the people, I admit that he expressed very good opinions. Just as he chose a very good wife. The Chinese people really need beautiful things too much.

Pleasant Rain and Bitter Rain 230

— Tang Tao

My first essay, submitted to "Free Talk," was called "Rain in My Hometown." It has been more than two years since I wrote that article, but my mood seems to be the same as it was two years ago. Whenever I mention rain, I always feel that it is suitable for the countryside, not for the city, suitable for spring and autumn, not for winter and summer, suitable for dusk, not for daytime. However, this is only in general terms. If I were by the seaside, I would like summer storms.

This is because love and hate also have to change with the environment.

In fact, my love for spring rain, autumn rain, dusk, and rain in the countryside is also related to my environment. I often browse through books, especially the rain poems of poets. After reading a lot, I actually transferred my preferences. "The clean and mournful rain falls at dusk" is of course already well-known, and "Unable to listen through the window, the sorrow is again at the time of lighting the lamp" can also express the mood at this time. Xiao Hanjie of the Yuan Dynasty wrote in his "Lang Tao Sha" poem:

Wet with the fragrance of late blooms, spring rain, spring chill, sprinkled on the window and filled the door with hidden orchids. Dismal and desolate, still dripping, creating many kinds of feelings. Like scattering pearl plates with sleet, on the upstairs veranda; the mournful tune of the plantain carries sorrow. Green moss covers the steps before the hall, who will see it when they wake up in the morning?

This is indeed a good poem about spring rain. In addition, such as: "Several fishermen return with their bamboo hats and nets, a flower seller goes with a raincoat on his shoulder." "Let the afternoon drizzle wash away my sorrows, warm up the cold night with bonfires, hearing the fine rain tapping at the window." "A lonely lamp makes dreams easily awakened, my heart is broken by the old tunes of the Tang palace, the sound is lost in the palace clocks, dripping into my sorrowful heart, autumn is like a slender beauty in a jade tower. Outside the misty railing, the wutong trees are urged to fall, with the west wind sending them to the painted tiles." What is chanted is exactly spring rain and autumn rain.

In songs, I remember a "Shou Yang Qu" by Ma Zhiyuan, which chants the night rain in Xiaoxiang. The lyrics say:

The fishing lights are dim, the traveler's dream returns, each drop breaks my heart. A lone boat at the fifth watch, ten thousand families, is the tears of a departing person.

Although it does not explicitly point out the season, in my opinion, if it is not the end of spring, it is probably the beginning of autumn, otherwise there would not be these sounds. What our poets like is the pathetic and serene.

However, there are naturally also people who like spring rain, autumn rain, dusk, and rain in the countryside, not just because of its pathetic and serene qualities. For example, farmers do. Living in the city, daily drinking and washing do not require rainwater, and asphalt roads and cement houses are definitely not places that can accommodate serene raindrops. Therefore, everyone mostly hates bitter rain. But the countryside is not like this. Farmers like rain, especially spring rain, autumn rain, and evening rain. However, their reasons for liking it are not as empty as those of poets. In the words of Mr. Lin Yutang, they are actually utilitarians, because spring and autumn are the seasons when crops need water, and rain in the evening does not hinder work. If it does not become a disaster, they never know bitter rain.

Moreover, on the contrary, in drought seasons, they still have to pray for rain. The current method of praying for rain in our countryside is to prepare drums and horns, run to a place dedicated to praying for rain, worship the Dragon King, and then capture living things in a muddy pond. The best thing is a snake, a turtle, mud carp, and fish are also good. If it is a turtle or a shrimp, then everyone thinks it is terrible, saying that this is a sign of drought.

However, in the past, it was not the same. Zhang Zongzi wrote in his "Tao An Meng Yi":

In July of the Ren Shen year, every village was rained on, and they dressed up as tide gods and sea ghosts every day, competing to spit on them. In my village, they dressed up as the Water Margin heroes, and said, the painters of the Water Margin, Long Mian and Song Xue, are not as good as Shi Nai'an, but if their faces are not painted with rouge, if their mustaches are not like silkworms, if their helmets are not made of paper, if their knives and staffs are not made of trees, if their tales are not fabricated, and if their intestines are not twisted, then they are eighty or ninety percent accurate. So they split up and went out in all directions, looking for short black men, looking for tall men, finding monks, finding fat monks, finding strong women, finding beautiful women, finding men with green faces, finding men with crooked heads, finding men with red hair, finding men with beautiful beards, finding men with big black faces, and finding men with red faces and long beards. They searched the city, and if they couldn't find them, they went to the suburbs, villages, mountains, remote areas, and neighboring prefectures and counties, and hired them at high prices, getting thirty-six people. The Liangshan heroes were all alive, approaching in a proper manner, with men and horses properly dressed and moving along. The onlookers intercepted and blocked them, wanting to see Wei Jie in person...

The current method of praying for rain, although very cautious, is very small-scale compared to the extravagance of the Ming Dynasty. Is this progress or regression? It is really hard to say. However, the views on praying for rain are still consistent throughout the ages. Yuan Zifu wrote in his "Xiang You Xian Ping":

In the summer, when there is a long drought, all parties inevitably pray for rain, and the rain that comes with it is mostly the water from the rivers and lakes that is rolled up by the dragon, not formed by the interaction of yin and yang. In the summer of the seventh year of Zhenghe in Huizhou, there was a heavy rain, and two fish fell on the roof of the Dianzhong Province Office. This matter can be seen in the Later Supplement to the National History. How can there be fish in the rain? This rain is undoubtedly the water from the rivers and lakes, rolled up by the dragon.

Although eight hundred years have passed, and now it seems that we do not hear of any fish falling on the roof of government offices, most people still hold the same view as Yuan Zifu regarding praying for rain, thinking that it is rolled up by dragons. What exactly is going on?

It is probably still very difficult to say!

However, although this is shallow, it is not mysterious. Compared to those who only know how to like the pathetic and serene qualities of spring rain, autumn rain, dusk, and rain in the countryside, they still have a more factual basis.

A Crowd of Blind Men 231

Shen Bao Local Supplement

The Dark Secrets of the Jimo County Government 232

— Meng Ruo

Amidst the nationwide crackdown on opium, a recent opium case occurred in Jimo County, with the perpetrators all being county government officials, which is truly regrettable. An Qingdao telegram on the 8th: Lu Han reported that the Jimo County government was full of dark secrets, and many officials were addicted to drugs and harbored opium dens. He secretly dispatched Yao Yijia with ten soldiers, who arrived in Jimo at 1:00 PM on the 7th, surrounded the county government and the Chamber of Commerce, and found a large number of opium and opium paraphernalia. County government secretary Song Danting fled, and the head of the finance section, Liu Minsheng, the clerk Sun Xitu, and the chief of public security, Li Shichang, were arrested. The head of the Chamber of Commerce, Hu Jiaren, escaped, and his son, Jia Zeng, was captured and tied up together, and sent to Jinan for interrogation.

The nature of this case is completely different from ordinary opium cases: First, the dark secrets occurred in the county government, the highest political organ of the county, which cannot be ignored. Second, public officials using drugs are clearly violating the law knowingly. Third, in addition to using drugs, they also harbor opium dens, which also constitutes the crime of dereliction of duty and malfeasance. Fourth, opium and opium paraphernalia were found in the county government, and the perpetrators were obviously using them openly, which is even more illegal. In addition, from the discovery of this case, we can see the corruption of the Jimo County officials and the darkness of the government. Fortunately, Chairman Han is impartial and strict in his handling of matters. Now that he has dispatched troops to arrest many county government officials, he should be able to handle this case according to the law, punish corrupt officials, and clarify county governance. However, in addition to the opium case, we must also pay attention to whether there are other criminal acts. Since public officials dare to harbor opium dens, it is difficult to guarantee that they will not commit other crimes. The escaped criminals should also be arrested as soon as possible, so as not to let them escape the law.

However, although the opium case in Jimo County is unfortunate, are there only a few secretaries and chiefs in the Jimo County government who are addicted to opium among the officials in our country? As for harboring opium dens, this situation is also not uncommon. Therefore, we believe that if the authorities are determined to eradicate the scourge of opium, they should first dismiss (or at least order to quit within a time limit) the public officials who are addicted to opium. If it is found that they are harboring opium dens, they should be severely punished. Because if they do not do so, officials cannot set an example, how can they influence the people. I wonder how Chairman Han will deal with the county government officials in this opium case.

A Drinking Party 233

— Ai Tu

When I was a child, I heard people talking about drinking parties all day long. However, what exactly is a drinking party? It seems like an extremely mysterious and incomprehensible mystery. This mysterious mystery grew with age, and even when I was studying in middle school, I still didn't understand it thoroughly. Now that I have left school, left home, and left the so-called happy family, which is actually a dark hole of an environment, and am flying freely like a nimble little bird in the circle of freedom, wandering to Shanghai and other small cities, yet this mystery still occupies my brain. After all, what exactly is it? So I felt an infinite mystery in it.

I had a very good opportunity to try it out. Therefore, a mysterious mystery that I couldn't understand could be explored in this opportunity. It seemed to be an indispensable page in my life history. I cherished it, and I happily and enthusiastically observed it.

It was the afternoon of the Mid-Autumn Festival. I followed a friend who taught in elementary school from the countryside to Gongyibu, because they had agreed to open a room in the Guanhai Restaurant on this day, and of course, to enjoy their youth and happiness as much as possible. However, as for me? I had never lived such a life. Even on the long and distant journey of wandering, I lived a lonely life. Therefore, I was holding such a swinging mood towards this fresh and lively life.

The destination had arrived, and we stepped onto the upper floor of the Guanhai Hotel. It was quiet here, perhaps a necessary result of the economic panic. Such a tall hotel had no business at all. Even on this good festival, there were not many young people who came to revel, only our group. When I stepped into the room, they were already playing mahjong with a snap, snap, snap. On a

Page 18

square table, each of the young people on each side was tightly stretching their flushed faces, and their eyes were calmly turning on the tiles. A waiter was serving tea and sending hot towels. Here, a row of windows faced south. The south was a railway station, a factory, and next to the restaurant was a flowing stream. From here, you could see a vast expanse of white river water, and in the distance, the mountain peaks, plains, and villages were shrouded in the clouds, all of which were silent. However, the liveliness in this room made me feel unfamiliar and unaccustomed, and I felt very sad in my heart. They were talking about their own things, laughing about their own things, and the stories about women they were talking about had no appeal to me at all. Therefore, although the people here were lively, I was obviously lonely, as if I were in another terrible world. Yes, if I had learned to play mahjong when I was a child, and had learned to do some so-called mysterious things, I think I would not have had such a terrible sadness as today. However, do I curse? I currently seem to be a prisoner enduring the irony in front of everyone's faces, terribly lonely.

With great difficulty, they finished four rounds, and it was already three o'clock in the afternoon. They talked about calling Meihua to accompany them to the drinking party. This, of course, I knew, and my heart rose with a strange desire again. After a while, Miss Meihua stepped into the room gracefully.

She did not refuse anyone's embrace, nor did she refuse anyone's kiss. Three young men whom I had never met, who lived a theatrical troupe life in Gongyi, were making music, singing and laughing, as if they had forgotten their pain. They all joked with her. So, the room seemed particularly lively, but I had become an idiot, thinking wildly. I was afraid, I was ashamed, I dared not approach her, and I dared not even look at her. Even I didn't believe that I was one of the group. However, sometimes when I saw their hands causing her chest to feel pain, she let out a mournful sound, which almost struck my soul. She dared not cry, nor dare curse, thus making their eyes flash with joyous brilliance.

Drinking and eating turned everyone as hot as fire. So, my soul burned up and down. After a while, they continued to play cards. She had taken turns at each position to help them for a while. The pain she endured, perhaps was also pleasure, and there were also sarcastic words. Continuing like this in the crazed circle, as for me, I seemed to be hearing the whip of the referee, just silently. This long evil play continued until two o'clock in the middle of the night, and I didn't even see a bit of a bright moon. Then I followed them to eat a midnight snack again. After eating the midnight snack, a group of young people dispersed, and I went to another room to lie down my tired body, thinking wildly—this night, she spent the night with that young man, maybe it was happy!

When I got up the next morning, I returned to her and his room. At that time, she ridiculed me like a loving mother; squinting her eyes and patting my shoulder:

"You kid, you don't understand anything, you've suffered in front of us."

Oh! My face turned red, and I left her speechless, but I already recognized this mysterious mystery, the drinking party, the sinful drinking party!!

Little Gleanings Under the Lamp 234

— Er He

(1) An Ancient Mirror

On the second night of returning to my hometown, I found an ancient mirror while tidying up my books. I was at a loss, as if I had lost everything. When I regained some clarity, I only felt a sour feeling in my eyes. Ah, this ancient mirror, this ancient mirror! Speaking to myself, tears dripped onto the ancient mirror. It was an ancient mirror left by my mother, but according to what my mother said when she was alive, it was brought from my maternal grandmother's side.

Therefore, the ancient mirror is of course an ancient mirror!

I still remember my maternal grandmother's gray hair. This ancient mirror, my maternal grandmother must have looked into. But where can I find my maternal grandmother's white hair at this moment? In the ancient mirror, I am reflected, a haggard, thin, and teary-eyed young man. My mother must have also looked into it. But where can I find my mother's shadow at this moment? In the ancient mirror, I am reflected, a haggard, thin, and teary-eyed young man.

When I was young, by my mother's side, I often competed with Fangmei for the ancient mirror. Everyone was happy to look at their playful and mischievous faces in the ancient mirror. A few years later, Fangmei passed away, and my mother also passed away. I drifted to a distant place like a lone goose. My father only loved to hold a long-stemmed pipe, and did not like to look in the mirror. Therefore, the ancient mirror was buried in the books.

This time, I unearthed the ancient mirror that had been buried for many years like an archaeologist. I was delighted, and I felt a strong sense of sadness, but who could I tell?

The mercury on the back of the mirror had faded, but after wiping away the dust on the surface of the mirror, the ancient mirror was still bright. Looking at it alone, looking at it, like a hero who had killed all the enemies, looking at his own bloody knife on an evening in late autumn, he felt lonely and desolate! As time goes on, this ancient mirror may fall into the hands of others. But at that time, who will be an archaeologist, who will recall my current haggard, thin, and teary-eyed face to one in ten thousand?

(2) Listening to the Wind

Most of the scenery of nature is suitable for seeing. You can see the brilliant sunset, you can see the brilliant rainbow with seven colors after the rain, you can see the shy flowers with dewdrops, and you can also see the vast expanse of misty waves for thousands of miles.

But I seem to be particularly happy to listen. I feel that listening is far better than seeing. I am of course happy to listen to a spring-singing oriole, to listen to the sound of cicadas in a tree in late autumn, to listen to the surging of a river of waves, and to listen to the sound of ten thousand raindrops hitting the roof, making the sound of shattered jade. But what makes me even happier is listening to the wind.

Move a deck chair in the garden, close your eyes, and listen to a gust of light wind passing through the green shade, the leaves rubbing against each other. This sound is so subtle, and this beautiful enjoyment of stillness in movement is far better than seeing.

In the evening, I often like to open the window and lie lonely in bed with my eyes closed, quietly listening to a gust of wind rushing up to the window, and then the pages of the book on the table turn over, one page after another, turning over and over again. I think this tedious sound is the best to listen to. Sometimes the curtains also flutter, which makes people think that their bed is a lone boat floating on the vast waves, and of course they are a lone guest on the lone boat. So, I open the flowers of memory and think of some stories from many years ago…

If it is a strong wind, and it is also in the middle of the night, then close the windows tightly and listen quietly in the dark as the wind attacks the jungle, like ten thousand horses galloping, like a tsunami turning over dragons, like a tiger roaring and a lion roaring. Calmly listen with bated breath, and gradually your hair will stand on end, and you will even be afraid to move, as if something dangerous will fall down immediately if you move. But the mind is not easy to calm down, it will think of the reefs of the Arctic Ocean, it will think of the wild beasts in the deep mountains, it will think of all kinds of alarming and frightening things…. Because it is listening, because the eyes are closed, so you will think of all kinds of things more than seeing.

Listening to the wind is indeed a joy for me.

One Night in Xuzhou (Continued) 235

— Menghua

Soon, we fell asleep. In my dream, I dreamed of this strange girl. I clearly saw her sparse bangs, her pale face, her slender body, and her mournful eyes. She also seemed to be complaining to me in a gloomy voice. She was crying, crying desperately...

In the morning, before the alarm clock that I brought with me rang, a burst of noise woke me up. In a daze, I vaguely heard a man shouting. I tried my best to open my very heavy eyelids and leaned up from the bed. In this way, I clearly heard a man's angry scolding and a woman's low weeping. In addition, there were many noisy voices, as if people were mediating.

At this moment, my friend walked into the room. Obviously, he had been awakened long ago.

"What exactly is going on with the noise outside?" I asked.

"That woman from last night had an accident." He said. "Get up quickly, it's time."

"Freezing to death will get us into trouble, what a joke!" The waiter shouted outside. "Damn it, black-hearted, you won't have a good reward in your life. She stayed up all night last night, she

Page 19

said that going back is death, and not going back is also death, so she would rather die here. This girl is also too tough."

"That's right, her cheekbones are on fire, burning red, and she's coughing." Another person said.

"What exactly is the matter?" I asked my friend, "Who is scolding her?"

"It's the 'turtle head'. He's also scolding the waiters in this inn. They almost beat him, fortunately I was there to mediate."

Suddenly, her gaunt face floated before my eyes again. This white rose in the storm.

"What if she had a guest last night?" I thought to myself, and unconsciously said it out loud.

My friend seemed not to have heard my words. He weighed the quilt with his hand and said in a self-satisfied tone:

"Hey, if it weren't for this quilt last night, I might have frozen to death in Xuzhou!"

Main Street 236

— Green Leaves

——Impressions of an Ancient City

On the main street, there is something special: tall windows and gray walls. The sun shines forlornly on the gray, sandy street, and on the plain cloth awnings of the cloth shops and wine houses against the gray sky. The street is filled with the "ka-dong, ka-dong" sound of rickshaw pullers' copper bells, forlornly echoing in the gray sand. This is life painted in gray, with that gray tone. The livelihood of an entire family revolves on those wheels.

The street is paved with gravel, and in the bright sunlight and wind, gray sand rolls along the ground, blurring in the air. Over there, I can see the gray, peeling city walls, and the drowsy, gray soldiers, with only the tips of their guns visible on the city walls. A few crows adorn this desolate scene, adding to the grayness.

The main street is desolate. A few women with children are watching the excitement or occasionally buying things, arguing with the shopkeepers over prices. At times, there are wanderers wandering on the main street for most of the day, harboring memories of their distant hometowns, and all day long, mediators, also gray, walk on the street, walking, walking.

Sometimes, on the main street, there is a ragged peddler, selling children's toys and candy. He manipulates the toys in his hands, shouting, and the children watch these interesting toys, their shiny black eyes fixed on the little tricks of the toy. So, they ask their mothers to buy one. The peddler is also clever. He knows exactly what the children want at this moment; he will follow closely beside the child, asking, and so, the mother buys the toy. This is an interesting scene in an ancient city.

Along the street are many fruit stalls and secondhand goods stalls. Beside the stalls are old, coughing men. They talk to each other, chatting about this and that, chatting about their sons and daughters-in-law for most of the day. There are also talkative ones who smoke their pipes all day long, chatting, and sometimes dealing with customers, passing the time.

I once spent five copper coins to buy a pear to quench my thirst, but I only took one bite before throwing it on the ground. The taste was bitter and astringent, and the inside was like cotton, filled with gray sand. Eating fruit in the ancient city is not a happy experience.

On the main street, you can buy anything, such as coal, cigarettes, wine, cloth, and small items for women, like buttons and thread. These are all more expensive than those sold in the alleys, which is the usual practice of the market. The main street is the most prosperous market in the ancient city. Now, the main street is desolate. There are no customers in the shops. Previously, the cloth shops were crowded with people, demanding a bit of cloth, just a cacophony of women's and men's voices. Now, the cloth shops are deserted. So much old stock is piled up in the shops, some even from Tokyo and Shanghai, flashing red and green in the sunlight. Young shop assistants are secretly dozing off at the counter. The market is declining: only desolation and grayness remain.

In the small theaters on the main street, many people seek a little warmth to comfort their hearts and add some color to the dullness of their gray lives. The main street, on the contrary, is lonely and deserted. Three or four stray dogs run down the street with their tails between their legs, and a broken rickety car drives through the street, "ta-da, ta-da." The big drum on the street also "de, de, de," bangs and bangs. This is also a special phenomenon in the market.

Broadcasting

New Song Introduction 237

Money is Omnipotent

Theme Song from the Shanghai Film Company's Sound Film "Peach Blossom Dream"

(The Emperor sings on his throne) Silver clouds gently illuminate the golden mountains, golden light brightly illuminates the waves of the world. Who can stem the raging tides? Without gold, there is nothing to eat; without silver, there is nothing to wear. Even if you are talented, handsome, meritorious, and virtuous, possessing everything, if you cannot amass and manage money, humph, humph! Your entire life will be incompetent, without fortune, power, or influence. Everyone will hate you, and everyone will dislike you, carrying your lifelong hardship to the underworld. (Everyone) We praise the omnipotence of money! Your Majesty, the Emperor, is all-powerful, with boundless magic, employing both grace and authority, accomplished in both civil and military affairs. Long live, long live, ten thousand long lives!

(Citizen A) Long live, grant justice! (Empress, in a white voice) What grievances do you have? (Citizen A) I am now carrying a heavy burden of a thousand gold. Year after year, I toil and suffer, year after year, I am hungry and cold. Alas, from morning till night, my wife complains and my children resent me. What a grievance! (The Empress summons the Money Arhat.) (Deity A) What is your command? (Empress) Quickly put steel plates on both sides of his face, so they are firm and thick, and he won't be ashamed. From now on, you will earn your meals and make money relying on a thick skin. Hey! Don't care about anything! (The crowd joins in singing the refrain)

(Citizen B) Long live, save my life! (Empress, in a white voice) What danger are you in? (Citizen B) I have spent effort and energy to obtain a high official position. I have collected miscellaneous taxes and levies with a loyal heart, fearing that everyone will rebel and kick me out. How dangerous! (The Empress summons the Silver Dollar Arhat.) (Deity B) What is your command? (Empress) Quickly replace his conscience with a lump of coal, so it is dirty and black, leaning to one side. From now on, you will loot and hoard money, causing families to be ruined and destroyed. Hey! Don't care about anything! (The crowd joins in singing the refrain)

(Citizen C) Long live, show mercy! (Empress, in a white voice) What difficulties are you facing? (Citizen C) Now the world's great powers have countless wealth. They continuously send in military supplies and transport them across the mountains and passes. Many high officials are daring, but I dare not do it. How miserable! (The Empress summons the Banknote Arhat.) (Deity C) What is your command? (Empress) Quickly put all the blood and sweat in his body into an ice pool, let it be cold, let it be hard, freezing his mind and heart. From now on, you will sell out the country and surrender to the enemy, becoming a traitor and a running dog. Hey! Don't care about anything! (The crowd joins in singing the refrain)

(Refrain) We praise the omnipotence of money! Your Majesty, the Emperor, is all-powerful, with boundless magic, possessing everything. What should we do? How should we do it? (Empress, singing alone) Do whatever you want! Golden light and silver vapor spread… (The crowd joins in singing) Do whatever you want! (Empress, singing alone) We will turn the world upside down… (The crowd joins in singing) Do whatever you want! (Empress, singing alone) We will make the seas run dry and the stones crumble! (The crowd joins in singing) Do whatever you want! (Singing together) It's not difficult!

Ballad Singing 239

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles

Dunben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening Piece "Butterfly Dream Marriage"

Silver candles shine in the frosted tent, filling it with fragrance. A young widow carefully puts on makeup. Suddenly, she sees an old servant arrive. Her brows lift with joy as she enters the painted hall. Madam, I will report to the young master that I am grateful for your kindness. First, put away the mourning garments and choose an auspicious day for the wedding. Old one, choosing a day is not as good as stumbling upon one. Why not complete the wedding tonight? I will fulfill my desire for a romantic affair. Arrange it quickly and enter the bridal chamber. Quickly go to the boudoir and put on your auspicious clothes. Let this old servant act as the master of ceremonies and invite the groom. Pay respects to heaven and earth, enter the bridal chamber, and sit shoulder to shoulder, hiding your faces with fans. Foolish Tian stealthily looks at him and sees him tightly frowning, tears filling his eyes. With a loud cry, she falls down, startling Tian in a panic. Old one, why is your young master acting like this? Quickly help the young man into bed. The young master has always had heart pain. No doctor in the world has a wonderful cure. China does have living human brains, and taking them will have a powerful effect. I'm afraid there are no brains here, and the scholar will die. Old one, can the newly deceased be used? If so, there is room for discussion. Madam, it can still be used before the seventh day. Taking it will have a quick and strong effect. Hearing this, Tian splits open the coffin.

Xing Ruiting's Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening Piece "Woman Cries for Agarwood"

Autumn scenery, the fragrance of osmanthus in August. A sentimental woman sits in her boudoir. All she hears is the endless chirping of insects outside the window, and the wind blowing the purple bamboo with a rustling sound. The iron horse on the eaves clashes. She lowers her head and thinks to herself. She thinks of the handsome and talented man from her maiden home. She has not been married to her husband for even half a month. A maid brings a letter to my room, saying that the talented man is sick in bed. I face the incense table and offer empty prayers, begging the heavens and the city god, hoping that he will be safe and healthy. I have not been married for even a month. A maid brings a letter to my room, saying that the talented man has passed away. It has made me cry to death several times and return to life. My husband asks me why I am so sad. I only say that the pain in my abdomen is the hardest to bear. I should be offering condolences before the spirit, but I am only a new bride who has not yet completed her first month of marriage, so it is inconvenient for me to attend the funeral. I can only secretly wear three parts of mourning and put a piece of hemp cloth on my chest. I don't wear red or green clothes, only two pieces of plain clothes. On a pair of arched shoes, I put hemp cloth. I send a maid to buy a piece of agarwood. I carve the talented man's handsome face. I carve him wearing a square scarf with fluttering ribbons, with white jade emitting light in the center. He wears a dark blue robe with a yellow belt, red satin shoes with black satin trim. I can't carve you pacing back and forth in the study. I can't carve you calling me "dear sister." I can't carve you playing chess and looking around. I can't carve you urging me several times to not separate because the wedding sedan is arriving at the hall. I have to harden my heart and say goodbye to the talented man. When I got into the sedan, I cried sadly. The idlers only gossiped, saying that I couldn't bear to leave my father and mother. Little did they know that I couldn't bear to leave the affectionate and righteous talented man. Talented man, I worship you on the dressing table during the day. In the evening, I use the green gauze curtain as a shrine. In this world, there are so many sad things. Others' sadness can be grieved. My sadness is hidden in my heart.

Fine Arts 240

Mao Zhizhong's Fine Arts Lecture

Hangye (1180) 5:30 PM to 6:15 PM

The qualities of painting: 1. Literati painting includes those by writers and epigraphers. 2. Famous painters have Southern and Northern schools. 3. Popular painting learns from everyone and does not distinguish between schools. Those who enter through the three categories of spirit, mystery, and ability belong to popular painting; those who do not belong to literati painting. Teaching painting: 3. Lectures on the biographies of painters.

Film

Xu Lai's Wonderful Performance 242

It is the season when the fragrance of osmanthus flowers fills the air. By the clear Zihu Lake, Xu Lai and her old father, for the sake of livelihood, shout loudly every day: "Hey! Is anyone going to Yue Fei's Tomb? Is anyone going to Yue Fei's Tomb?"

Of course, such a beautiful woman will secretly be coveted by others. In this place, there is a philandering man who calls himself an artist, Sun Min.

Spring does not last long, and the weather gradually turns to late autumn. When artists and travelers come to Hangzhou to appreciate the scenery, Xu Lai's old father's old illness recurs and he cannot operate the boat. As a result, the boat rental is overdue. The fat Tan Zhiyuan, who manages a dozen boats, urges them every day. Sun Min takes this opportunity to bribe him and uses the means of demanding money to coerce them. If they don't have money to repay the debt, Xu Lai must be a "model" once. So, in a helpless situation, Xu Lai had to make her sacred body an object of appreciation for beauty—the beautiful shadow in the painting.

This scene is Xu Lai's most wonderful performance in the monster Shen Xiling's film "Boat Girl."

MGM's Grand Musical Film "The Great Ziegfeld" Premieres 243

Isn't the "Les Misérables" currently showing in Nanjing a huge sensation for audiences at sea? However, the MGM musical opera that follows "Les Misérables" should win the general welcome and praise of movie fans at sea even more so; because "The Great Ziegfeld" has brought together Elena Powell, the most famous Tartar dance saint and diva in Europe and America, Jack Benny, the originator of humorous radio broadcasts, and 200 newly selected song and dance beauties, as well as 15 MGM stars, to jointly perform the 1936-style American art song and dance, which can be called an unprecedented creation of the 20th century. As for the seven-year production and the millions of dollars spent on scenery, it is only an extra matter for this great song and dance film. The left is one of the singing and dancing scenes in the film.
